certification of the petition to repeal the ordinance being referred to the voters. In the event the
Council repeals the ordinance, the referendum petition shall be declared null and void.
2. If the petition is an initiative petition, the City Council shall have thirty (30) days to pass an
ordinance substantially as proposed by the petition. In the event the Council passes such an
ordinance, the initiative petition shall be null and void.
3. In the event the City Council neither repeals the ordinance which is the subject of a referendum
petition, nor enacts an ordinance which is the subject of an initiative petition, an election shall be
ordered by the City Clerk to be conducted City-wide. A special election for initiative or
referendum shall be provided not more than ninety (90) days following the certification of the
petition, provided that in the event a City election will occur within the ninety (90) days, the
initiative or referendum shall be submitted at the time of the City election. (Ord. 520, 10-10-1977)
1-12-9: FORM OF BALLOT:
A. Ways Of Preparing Ballot: The City Council shall prepare a ballot for an initiative or referendum
election in one of the following ways:
1. If the full text of the ordinance or proposed ordinance to be voted upon does not exceed thirty
(30) words in length, it may be set out in full on the election ballot; or
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 35/315
2. If the full text of the ordinance or proposed ordinance to be voted upon exceeds thirty (30) words
in length, and the Council votes not to have it printed at length on the election ballot, it shall, with
the assistance of the City Attorney, prepare a short title and description of the ordinance or
proposed ordinance which shall clearly and impartially state its purpose and effect, which short
title and description shall be printed on the election ballot.
B. Initiative Election Ballot: After the initiative election ballot has been prepared as set forth herein,
there shall be printed the following instructions to the voter:
"To vote on the initiative make a mark in the square at the right of yes or no" and immediately
thereunder the question "Shall the ordinance set forth herein be enacted?" and immediately to the
right of such question shall be printed the word "Yes" and "No" not less than three-sixteenths (3/16)
of an inch in height and at the right of "Yes" and at the right of "No" a square shall be printed on the
ballot in which the voter may indicate his preference.
C. Referendum Election Ballot: After the referendum election ballot has been prepared as set forth
herein, there shall be printed the following instructions to the voter:
"To vote on the referendum make a mark in the square at the right of yes or no", and
immediately thereunder the question "Shall the ordinance set forth herein be retained?" and
immediately to the right of such question shall be printed the word "Yes" and "No" not less than
three-sixteenths (3/16) inch in height and at the right of "Yes" and at the right of "No" a square shall
be printed on the ballot in which the voter may indicate his preference.
(Ord. 520, 10-10-1977)
1-12-10: CONDUCT OF ELECTION:
Initiative or referendum elections, whether special or general, shall be conducted and the results
thereof canvassed and certified in all respects as near as practicable, in like manner as general
elections, except as otherwise provided. (Ord. 520, 10-10-1977)
1-12-11: CANVAS OF RETURNS:
The Mayor and Council shall meet within five (5) days after said election to canvas the votes cast at
such election, and the City Clerk shall immediately announce the results. Any initiative measure
approved by a majority of the votes cast shall be in full force and effect from the date of such
announcement. Any ordinance which is the subject of a referendum receiving less than a majority of
the votes cast shall be repealed, effective on the date of such announcement. (Ord. 520, 10-10-1977)
1-12-12: PROHIBITED ACTS; PENALTIES:
A person is guilty of a misdemeanor who:
A. Signs any name other than his own to an initiative or referendum petition.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 36/315
B. Knowingly signs his name more than once on the same initiative or referendum petition.
C. Knowingly signs his name to an initiative or referendum petition if he is not a registered City elector.
D. Wilfully or knowingly circulates, publishes or exhibits any false statement or representation
concerning the contents, purport or effect of any initiative or referendum petition for the purpose of
obtaining any signature to any such petition, or for the purpose of persuading any person to sign
any such petition.
E. Presents to any officer for filing any initiative or referendum petition to which is attached, appended
or subscribed any signature which the person so filing such petition knows to be false or
fraudulent, or not the genuine signature of the person purporting to sign such petition, or whose
name is attached, appended or subscribed thereto.
F. Circulates or causes to circulate any initiative or referendum petition, knowing the same to contain
false, forged or fictitious names.
G. Makes any false affidavit concerning any initiative or referendum petition or the signatures
appended thereto.
H. Offers, proposes or threatens for any pecuniary reward or consideration:
1. To offer, propose, threaten or attempt to sell, hinder or delay any initiative or referendum petition
or any part thereof or any signature thereon.
2. To offer, propose or threaten to desist from beginning, promoting or circulating any initiative or
referendum petition.
3. To offer, propose, attempt or threaten in any manner or form to use any recall petition or any
power of promotion or opposition in any manner or form for extortion, blackmail or secret or
private intimidation of any person or business interest. (Ord. 520, 10-10-1977)
Chapter 13
ELEVATIONS
1-13-1: ESTABLISHMENT OF ELEVATIONS:
All official elevations hereafter established in the City shall be described with reference to their
elevation as compared with the official base in feet and decimal parts of a foot, no grade or official
elevation shall be established other than by ordinance and in the manner described in this Chapter.
(Ord. 282, 9-12-1949)
1-13-2: BASE POINT ESTABLISHED:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 37/315
For the purpose of establishing grades in the streets, avenues, alleys and block intersections in the
City, the following datum point shall be taken as a base, or starting point:
The brass USGS bench mark situated in the northeast abutment of the Orofino Creek Bridge on
Johnson Avenue as now located, the elevation of said point being one thousand sixteen feet
(1016.00') above sea level. (Ord. 282, 9-12-1949)
Chapter 14
OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER
1-14-1: OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER:
The Clearwater Tribune, a weekly newspaper published within the City, is hereby designated as the
official newspaper of the City. (1962 Code)
Chapter 15
DEPOSITORY
1-15-1: DEPOSITORY DESIGNATED:
The official depository for the city of Orofino is hereby designated as U.S. Bank. (Ord. 740, 8-12-2008)
1-15-2: INSUFFICIENT FUNDS CHECKS:
A service charge of twenty dollars ($20.00) to be assessed for each check issued and deposited in the
official depository by an individual, company, or other for which there are insufficient funds (monies) in
the bank or other applicable financial institution to cover the amount of said check(s). (Ord. 740, 8-12-
2008)
1-15-3: AMENDMENTS:
The city council is authorized to amend any portion of this chapter by a resolution. (Ord. 740, 8-12-
2008)

Title 2
COMMISSIONS AND BOARDS
Chapter 1
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
2-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this Chapter:
COMMISSION: The Planning and Zoning Commission created by this Chapter.
COUNCIL: The Council of the City of Orofino.
IMPACT AREA: The area of City impact described in Section 11-4-3 of this City Code.
MEMBERS: All voting members of the Commission. (Ord. 544, 4-22-1980)
2-1-2: CREATION; MEMBERSHIP:
A. Membership; Term: The Commission shall consist of seven (7) members appointed by the Mayor
and confirmed by the Council. All members must have been residents of the City or of Clearwater
County (impact area member) for at least two (2) years immediately preceding appointment and
must reside within the City or within the impact area while serving on the Commission. The term of
office for the members shall be six (6) years, except that three (3) of the seven (7) members
initially appointed shall serve terms of only three (3) years. (Ord. 693, 1-24-2000)
B. Vacancies; Compensation: All vacancies shall be filled for the balance of the term vacated in the
same manner as original appointments. Members shall be selected without respect to political
affiliations and shall serve without compensation.
C. Resignation, Removal Of Members: Any member who is absent from three (3) consecutive regular
meetings or five (5) regular meetings during a single calendar year shall be deemed to have
resigned. Such resignations shall be effective the day immediately following the third consecutive
regular meeting absence or the fifth regular meeting absence during a calendar year. Members
may be removed for cause by an absolute majority vote of the Council. (Ord. 544, 4-22-1980)
2-1-3: RULES; ORGANIZATION AND MEETINGS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 44/315
The Commission shall elect a chairman and shall create and fill such offices as it may determine
necessary. Meetings of the Commission shall be held when duly called by the chairman by written or
oral notice. At least one regular meeting shall be held each month for not less than nine (9) months in
a year. A majority of members of the Commission shall constitute a quorum. All meetings shall be
open to the public. Written rules consistent with this Chapter and the laws of the State for the
transaction of business of the Commission shall be adopted. Written records of meetings, hearings,
resolutions, findings, studies, permits and actions shall be maintained at the office of the City Clerk
and shall be open to the public. The Commission shall have a reasonable time, to be set by the
Council, within which to examine and consider such actions as are required by this Chapter. (Ord.
544, 4-22-1980)
2-1-4: DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the Planning and Zoning Commission to:
A. Conduct a planning process designed to prepare, implement, review and update at least once
annually a comprehensive plan that includes all lands within the City limits, and in the impact area
pursuant to sections 67-6508 and 67-6509, Idaho Code;
B. Hold public hearings prior to recommendations pertaining to the comprehensive plan, changes to
the plan, and ordinances relative thereto;
C. Provide ways and means to obtain citizen participation in the planning process;
D. Recommend to Council subdivision and zoning ordinances;
E. Recommend to Council any changes to the comprehensive plan and zoning ordinances prior to the
annexation of an unincorporated area;
F. Recommend to Council a map, a governing plan and ordinances for the City and the impact area;
G. Provide ways and means to obtain citizen participation in the administration of the duties of the
Commission including, but not limited to, appointing nonvoting ex officio advisors, establishing
subcommittees and advisory committees, and organizing neighborhood groups;
H. Prepare procedures for processing zoning permits, special use permits, rezoning applications,
planned unit development proposals and variance applications;
I. Hear all requests for amendments to the zoning ordinances, hold at least one public hearing
thereon, and make recommendations to Council;
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 45/315
J. Recommend to Council changes to the zoning ordinances which the Commission deems
appropriate;
K. Recommend to Council the adoption of coordinated plans for the physical development of the City;
L. Recommend to Council the formation of zoning districts;
M. Make recommendations to Council concerning the layout, design, widening, extending and locating
the streets, roads and highways for relief of traffic;
N. Make recommendations to Council concerning the density of population and development of land
within the City;
O. Make recommendations to Council concerning the future growth, development and beautification of
the City in respect to its public buildings, streets, parks, grounds and land consistent with the future
growth and development of the City and the impact area in order to promote the public health,
morals, safety and welfare of the inhabitants thereof;
P. Make recommendations to Council for legislation and regulations concerning the landscaping and
the location of buildings, structures, or works to be erected, constructed, or altered and to give
suggestions and advice to individuals concerning such landscaping and the location of buildings,
structures, or works to be erected, constructed, or altered;
Q. Hear all applications for special exceptions, special uses, zoning changes and/or variances and
make recommendations to Council thereon; provided, that the Commission shall not submit such
recommendations to Council until a public hearing is held at which interested persons shall have
an opportunity to be heard following notice as provided in Sections 11-2-14, 11-2-15, 11-2-16, and
11-2-17 of this Code as is applicable;
R. With the consent of the owner, through its members, officers, agents and employees, in the
performance of their functions, enter upon any land and make examinations and surveys and place
and maintain necessary monuments and marks thereon;
S. Consider and pass upon all maps, plats and re-plats of lands which require the approval of the
Council. Any and all maps, plats and re-plats shall be first submitted to the Commission for its
consideration and recommendation to the Council; and
T. Perform any other duties deemed appropriate by Council which do not conflict with the laws of
Idaho. (Ord. 544, 4-22-1980)
2-1-5: EXPENDITURES:
With approval of the Council, the Commission may receive and expend funds, goods and services
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 46/315
from the Federal Government or agencies and instrumentalities of the State or local governments or
from civic and private sources and may contract with said entities and provide information and reports
as necessary to secure aid. Any expenditures of the Commission shall, exclusive of gifts, be within the
amount appropriated and set aside, from time to time, by Council, for purposes of the Commission as
set forth in this Chapter. Within such limits the Commission is authorized to hire employees and
technical advisers, including, but not limited to, planners, engineers, architects and legal assistants.
(Ord. 544, 4-22-1980)
2-1-6: CONFLICTS OF INTEREST:
No member or employee of the Council or the Commission shall participate in any proceeding or
action when the member or employee or his employer, business partner, business associate or any
person related to him by affinity or consanguinity within the second degree has an economic interest
in any proceeding shall be disclosed at or before any meeting at which the action is being heard or
conducted. (Ord. 544, 4-22-1980)
Title 3
DEPARTMENTS
Chapter 1
POLICE DEPARTMENT
3-1-1: DEPARTMENT CREATED:
There is hereby created a Police Department which shall consist of the Chief of Police and such other
personnel as may be provided by the City Council. (Ord. 278, 8-12-1949)
3-1-2: DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the members of the Police Department to see to the enforcement of all of the
laws of the City and all statutes applicable therein; and to preserve order and prevent infractions of the
law and arrest violators thereof. (1962 Code)
3-1-3: WITNESS FEE:
Every member of the Police Department shall appear as witness whenever necessary in a prosecution
for a violation of any law or of any State or Federal law. No such member shall retain any witness fee
for service as witness in any action or suit to which the City is a party; any fees paid for such services
shall be turned over to the Chief of Police, who shall deposit the same with the Treasurer. (1962
Code)
3-1-4: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 47/315
The Chief of the Police Department may make or prescribe such rules and regulations as he shall
deem advisable; such rules, when approved by the City Council, shall be binding on such members.
Such rules and regulations may cover, besides the conduct of the members, uniforms and equipment
to be worn or carried, hours of service, vacations and all other similar matters necessary or desirable
for the better efficiency of the Department. (1962 Code)
3-1-5: MATRON:
The Mayor, with the consent of the Council, may appoint a Police Matron, who shall perform such
duties as may be assigned to her by the Chief of Police or by the Mayor. (1962 Code)
3-1-6: REWARDS:
The Chief of Police, for meritorious service rendered by any member of the police force in the due
discharge of his duty, may permit such member to retain for his own benefit, so far as he may be
permitted by law, any reward or present tendered him therefor, and it shall be cause of removal for any
member of the force to receive any such reward or present without notice thereof to the Chief of Police
and without his permission. (1962 Code)
Chapter 2
FIRE DEPARTMENT
3-2-1: DEPARTMENT CREATED:
There is hereby created a Fire Department which shall consist of a Fire Chief and such other
personnel as may be provided for by the Mayor and Council of the City. (1962 Code)
3-2-2: DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of members of the Fire Department to provide for the immediate answering of all
fire calls and to fight all fires in the best and most modern available methods. Members shall see to
the care and maintenance of all firefighting equipment and have such equipment in constant workable
condition at all times. (1962 Code)
3-2-3: FIRE PREVENTION:
Every possible action shall be taken by the members of the Fire Department to eliminate fire hazards
and to provide for fire prevention methods and operations within the City. (1962 Code)
3-2-4: VOLUNTEER MEMBERS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 48/315
All volunteer members of the Fire Department shall conduct themselves in the same manner and
under the same rules and regulations as regular members of the Department. They shall respond to
all fire calls according to a schedule prescribed by the Chief of the Fire Department and they shall
attend all meetings and drills called by the Chief. (1962 Code)
Title 4
BUILDING REGULATIONS
Chapter 1
BUILDING CODE
4-1-1: CODES ADOPTED:
A. International Building Code: The international building code, 2012 edition, prepared by the
International Code Council, Inc., as adopted by the state of Idaho or the Idaho building code board,
together with any amendments or revisions to the international building code through the
negotiated rulemaking process is adopted.
B. International Residential Code: The international residential code, 2009 edition, prepared by the
International Code Council, Inc., as adopted by the state of Idaho or the Idaho building code board,
together with any amendments or revisions to the international residential code through the
negotiated rulemaking process is adopted.
C. International Energy Conservation Code: The international energy conservation code, 2009 edition,
prepared by the International Code Council, Inc., as adopted by the state of Idaho or the Idaho
building code board, together with any amendments or revisions to the international energy
conservation code through the negotiated rulemaking process is adopted. (Ord. 780, 1-14-2014)
4-1-2: VIOLATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to erect, construct, enlarge, alter, repair, move,
improve, remove, convert or demolish, equip, use, occupy or maintain any building or structure in the
city, or cause the same to be done, contrary to or in violation of any of the provisions of the codes
adopted in this chapter.
Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of the codes adopted in this chapter
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and each such person shall be deemed guilty of a separate
offense for each and every day or portion thereof during which any violation of any of the provisions of
the codes adopted in this chapter is committed, continued or permitted. Upon the conviction of any
such violation, such persons shall be punishable by a fine of not more than three hundred dollars
($300.00), or by imprisonment of not more than thirty (30) days, or by both such fine and
imprisonment. (Ord. 780, 1-14-2014)

Chapter 3
SIGN CODE
4-3-1: ADOPTION OF CODE:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of regulating and controlling signs within the city of Orofino,
Idaho, the uniform sign code, 1997 edition and all future editions and amendments. (Ord. 698, 3-26-
2001)
4-3-2: ADMINISTRATION:
The building official shall have the power and duty to enforce the provisions of this chapter; and all
fees herein shall be paid into the city treasury. (Ord. 698, 3-26-2001)
4-3-3: INTERPRETATION:
Whenever in the building regulations it is provided that anything must be done to the approval of or
subject to the direction of the building official or any other designated representative of the city, this
shall be construed to give such officer only the discretion of determining whether the rules and
standards established by this chapter have been complied with, and no such provision shall be
construed as giving any other officer discretionary powers as to what such regulations and standards
shall be, or power to require conditions not prescribed by this chapter, or to enforce any law provisions
in any arbitrary or discriminatory manner. (Ord. 698, 3-26-2001)
4-3-4: VIOLATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to erect, construct, enlarge, alter, repair, move,
improve, remove, or convert any sign in the city, or cause the same to be done, contrary to or in
violation of any of the provisions of this code. Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the
provisions of this code shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and each such person shall be
deemed guilty of a separate offense for each and every day or portion thereof during which any
violation of the provisions of this code is committed, continued or permitted. Upon the conviction of
any such violation, such person shall be punished by a fine of not more than three hundred dollars
($300.00), or by imprisonment of not more than thirty (30) days, or by both such fine and
imprisonment. (Ord. 698, 3-26-2001)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 50/315
4-3-5: SIZE:
No sign within the city limits of Orofino shall exceed one hundred (100) square feet in size. If more
than one sign is placed on the same sign structure, the aggregate size of all signs shall not exceed
one hundred (100) square feet. (Ord. 698, 3-26-2001)
4-3-6: HEIGHT:
No sign or sign structure shall exceed twenty five feet (25') in height from the base of the ground to
the top of the sign or sign structure. (Ord. 698, 3-26-2001)
4-3-7: SPECIAL USE:
All signs or sign structures not meeting the requirements of the uniform sign code or the size and
height limitation of this chapter may apply for a special use permit through the city planning and
zoning commission. (Ord. 698, 3-26-2001)
4-3-8: PERMIT FEES:
Permit fees shall be as follows:
$50.00 for signs up to 100 square feet
50.00 for all signs that are approved under a special use permit
(Ord. 698, 3-26-2001)
Chapter 4
DANGEROUS BUILDINGS
4-4-1: DEFINITION:
All buildings or structures which have any or all of the following defects shall be deemed "dangerous
buildings":
A. Those whose interior walls or other vertical structural members list, lean or buckle to such an extent
that a plumb line passing through the center of gravity falls outside of the middle third of its base.
B. Those which, exclusive of the foundation, show thirty three percent (33%) or more, of damage or
deterioration of the supporting member or members, or fifty percent (50%) of damage or
deterioration of the nonsupporting enclosing or outside walls or covering.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 51/315
C. Those which have improperly distributed loads upon the floor or roof or in which the same are
overloaded or which have insufficient strength to be reasonably safe for the purpose used.
D. Those which have been damaged by fire, wind or other causes so as to have become dangerous to
life, safety, morals, or the general health and welfare of the occupants or the people of the City.
E. Those which have become or are so dilapidated, decayed, unsafe, unsanitary or which so utterly
fail to provide the amenities essential to decent living that they are unfit for human habitation or are
likely to cause sickness or disease, so as to work injury to the health, morals, safety or general
welfare of those living therein.
F. Those having light, air and sanitation facilities which are inadequate to protect the health, morals,
safety or general welfare of those living therein.
G. Those having inadequate facilities for egress in case of fire or panic or those having insufficient
stairways, elevators, fire escapes,or other means of communication.
H. Those which have parts thereof which are so attached that they may fall and injure members of the
public or property.
I. Those which because of their condition are unsafe, unsanitary, or dangerous to the health, morals,
safety or general welfare of the people of the City.
J. Those buildings existing in violation of any provision of the Building Code of this City, or any
provision of the Fire Prevention Code, or other ordinances of this City. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-2: STANDARDS FOR REPAIR, VACATION OR DEMOLITION:
The following standards shall be followed in substance by the Building Inspector and the Mayor and
Council in ordering repair, vacation or demolition:
A. If the dangerous building can reasonably be repaired so that it will no longer exist in violation of the
terms of this Chapter, it shall be ordered repaired.
B. If the dangerous building is in such condition as to make it dangerous to the health, morals, safety,
or general welfare of its occupants, it shall be ordered to be vacated.
C. In any case where a dangerous building is fifty percent (50%) damaged or decayed, or deteriorated
from its original value or structure, it shall be demolished, and in all cases where a building cannot
be repaired so that it will no longer exist in violation of the terms of this Chapter, it shall be
demolished. In all cases where a dangerous building is a fire hazard existing or erected in violation
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 52/315
of the terms of this Chapter or any ordinance of the City or statute of the State, it shall be
demolished. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-3: NUISANCES:
All dangerous buildings within the terms of Section 4-4-1 of this Chapter are hereby declared to be
public nuisances, and shall be repaired, vacated or demolished as hereinbefore and hereinafter
provided. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-4: DUTIES OF BUILDING INSPECTOR:
The Building Inspector shall have the power to:
A. Inspections Semi-Annually: Inspect or cause to be inspected semi-annually, including, but not
limited to, all buildings, schools, halls, churches, theaters, hotels, tenements, commercial,
manufacturing, residential, agricultural or loft buildings for the purpose of determining whether any
conditions exist which render such place a dangerous building within the terms of Section 4-4-1 of
this Chapter.
B. Inspection Upon Complaint: Inspect any building, wall or structure about which complaints are filed
by any person to the effect that a building, wall or structure is or may be existing in violation of this
Chapter.
C. Inspection Following Reports Of Police And Fire Departments: Inspect any building, wall or
structure reported (as hereinafter provided for) by the Fire or Police Departments of the City as
probably existing in violation of the terms of this Chapter.
D. Notify Property Owner Or Occupant Of Violation: Notify in writing the owner, occupant, lessee,
mortgagee, agent and all other persons having an interest in said building as shown by the land
records of the Recorder of Clearwater County, of any building found by him to be a dangerous
building within the standards set forth in Section 4-4-1 of this Chapter, that:
1. The owner must vacate, or repair, or demolish said building in accordance with the terms of the
notice and this Chapter;
2. The occupant or lessee must vacate said building or may have it repaired in accordance with the
notice and remain in possession;
3. The mortgagee, agent or other persons having an interest in said building as shown by the land
records of the Recorder of Clearwater County may at his own risk repair, vacate, or demolish
said building or have such work or act done; provided, that any person notified under this
subsection to repair, vacate, or demolish any building shall be given such reasonable time, not
exceeding thirty (30) days, as may be necessary to do, or have done, the work or act required by
the notice provided for herein.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 53/315
E. Contents Of Notice: Set forth in the notice provided for in subsection D of this Section, a description
of the building or structure deemed unsafe, a statement of the particulars which make the building
or structure a dangerous building and an order requiring the same to be put in such condition as to
comply with the terms of this Chapter within such length of time, not exceeding thirty (30) days, as
is reasonable.
F. Report Noncompliance: Report to the Mayor and Council any noncompliance with the notice
provided for in subsections D and E of this Section.
G. Appear At Hearings: Appear at all hearings conducted by the Mayor and Council, and testify as to
the condition of dangerous buildings.
H. Place Notice On Building: Place a notice on all dangerous buildings reading as follows:
This building has been found to be a dangerous building by the Building Inspector. This notice is
to remain on this building until it is repaired, vacated, or demolished in accordance with the notice
which has been given the owner, occupant, lessee, mortgagee, or agent of this building and all
other persons having an interest in said building as shown by the land records of the County
Recorder of Clearwater County, Orofino, Idaho. It is unlawful to remove this notice until such notice
is complied with.
(Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-5: DUTIES OF MAYOR AND COUNCIL:
The Mayor and Council shall:
A. Notify Property Owner Or Occupant To Appear: Upon receipt of a report of the Building Inspector as
provided for in subsection 4-4-4F of this Chapter, give written notice to the owner, occupant,
mortgagee, lessee, agent, and all other persons having an interest in said building as shown by the
land records of the Recorder of Clearwater County to appear before them on the date specified in
the notice to show cause why the building or structure reported to be a dangerous building should
not be repaired, vacated, or demolished in accordance with the statement of particulars as set forth
in the Building Inspector's notice provided for herein in subsection 4-4-4E.
B. Hold Hearing: Hold a hearing and hear such testimony as the Building Inspector or the owner,
occupant, mortgagee, lessee, or any other person having an interest in said building as shown by
the land records of the Recorder of Clearwater County shall offer relative to the dangerous
building.
C. Written Findings: Make written findings of fact from the testimony offered pursuant to subsection B
of this Section as to whether or not the building in question is a dangerous building within the terms
of Section 4-4-1 of this Chapter.
D. Issue Order: Issue an order based upon findings of fact made pursuant to subsection C of this
Section commanding the owner, occupant, mortgagee, lessee, agent and all other persons having
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 54/315
an interest in said building as shown by the land records of the Recorder of Clearwater County, to
repair, vacate, or demolish any building found to be a dangerous building within the terms of this
Chapter; and provided, that any person so notified, except the owners, shall have the privilege of
either vacating or repairing said dangerous building or any person not the owner of said dangerous
building but having an interest in said building as shown by the land records of the Recorder of
Clearwater County may demolish said dangerous building at his own risk to prevent the acquiring
of a lien against the land upon which said dangerous building stands by the City as provided in
subsection E hereof.
E. Abatement By City; Assessment Of Costs: If the owner, occupant, mortgagee, or lessee fails to
comply with the order provided for in subsection D of this Section, within ten (10) days, the Mayor
and Council shall cause such building or structure to be repaired, vacated, or demolished as the
facts may warrant, under the standards hereinbefore provided in Section 4-4-2 of this Chapter, and
shall with the assistance of the City Attorney cause the costs of such repair, vacation, or demolition
to be charged against the land on which the building existed as a Municipal lien or cause such
costs to be added to the tax duplicate as an assessment, or to be levied as a special tax against
the land upon which the building stands or did stand, or to be recovered in a suit at law against the
owner; provided, that in cases where such procedure is desirable and any delay thereby caused
will not be dangerous to the health, morals, safety, or general welfare of the people of the City, the
Mayor and Council shall notify the City Attorney to take legal action to force the owner to make all
necessary repairs or demolish the building.
F. Report Violators To Attorney: Report to the City Attorney the names of all persons not complying
with the order provided for in subsection D of this Section. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-6: VIOLATIONS; PENALTY:
A. Violation By Owner: The owner of any dangerous building who shall fail to comply with any notice
or order to repair, vacate or demolish said building given by any person authorized by this Chapter
to give such notice or order shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. A separate offense shall be deemed
committed upon each day such failure to comply continues beyond the date fixed for compliance.
B. Violation By Occupant: The occupant or lessee in possession who fails to comply with any notice to
vacate and who fails to repair said building in accordance with any notice given as provided for in
this Chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. A separate offense shall be deemed committed
upon each day such failure to comply continues beyond the date fixed for compliance.
C. Removal Of Notice From Building: Any person removing the notice provided in subsection 4-4-4H
of this Chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-7: DUTIES OF CITY ATTORNEY:
The City Attorney shall:
A. Prosecute Violators: Prosecute all persons failing to comply with the terms of the notices provided
for herein in subsections 4-4-4D and E of this Chapter and the order provided for in subsection 4-
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 55/315
4-5D of this Chapter.
B. Appear At Hearings: Appear at all hearings before the Mayor and Council in regard to dangerous
buildings.
C. Suits To Collect City Liens: Bring suit to collect all City liens, assessments, or costs incurred by the
Mayor and Council in repairing or causing to be vacated or demolished dangerous buildings.
D. Other Legal Actions: Take such other legal action as is necessary to carry out the terms and
provisions of this Chapter. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-8: EMERGENCY CASES:
In cases where it reasonably appears that there is immediate danger to the life or safety of any person
unless a "dangerous building" as defined herein is immediately repaired, vacated, or demolished, the
Building Inspector shall report such facts to the Mayor and Council, and the Mayor and Council shall
cause the immediate repair, vacation or demolition of such dangerous building. The costs of such
emergency repair, vacation or demolition of such dangerous building shall be collected in the same
manner as provided in subsection 4-4-5E of this Chapter. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-9: OWNER ABSENT FROM CITY:
In cases, except emergency cases, where the owner, occupant, lessee, or mortgagee is absent from
the City all notices or orders provided for herein shall be sent by certified mail to the owner, occupant,
mortgagee, lessee, and all other persons having an interest in said building as shown by the land
records of the Recorder of Clearwater County to the last known address of each, and a copy of such
notice shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the dangerous building to which it relates. Such
mailing and posting shall be deemed adequate service. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-10: ADMINISTRATIVE LIABILITY:
No officer, agent or employee of the City shall render himself personally liable for any damage that
may occur to persons or to property as a result of any act required or permitted in the discharge of his
duties under this Chapter. Any suit brought against any officer, agent or employee of the City as a
result of any act required or permitted in the discharge of his duties under this Chapter shall be
defended by the City Attorney until the final determination of the proceedings therein. (Ord. 397, 6-13-
1966)
4-4-11: DUTIES OF FIRE DEPARTMENT:
The employees of the Fire Department shall make a report in writing to the Building Inspector of all
buildings or structures which are, may be, or are suspected to be dangerous buildings within the terms
of this Chapter. Such reports must be delivered to the Building Inspector within twenty four (24) hours
of the discovery of such buildings by any employee of the Fire Department. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 56/315
4-4-12: DUTIES OF POLICE DEPARTMENT:
All employees of the Police Department shall make a report in writing to the Building Inspector of any
buildings or structures which are, may be, or are suspected to be dangerous buildings within the terms
of this Chapter. Such reports must be delivered to the Building Inspector within twenty four (24) hours
of the discovery of such buildings by any employee of the Police Department. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
4-4-13: SEPARABILITY:
It is the intention of the Council that each separate provision of this Chapter shall be deemed
independent of all other provisions herein, and it is further the intention of the Council that if any
provision of this Chapter be declared invalid, all other provisions hereof shall remain valid and
enforceable. (Ord. 397, 6-13-1966)
Chapter 5
GAS CODE
4-5-1: TITLE:
This Chapter shall be known as the GAS ORDINANCE OF OROFINO, IDAHO, and may be cited as
such. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this Chapter is to provide minimum standards, provisions, and requirements for safe
installation of gas appliances and gas pipes, and to regulate the sale, maintenance, and repair of such
appliances. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-3: SCOPE:
Any and all gas appliances or gas pipes hereafter sold, installed, maintained, or repaired within the
corporate limits shall conform to the requirements of this Chapter. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-4: DEFINITIONS:
The following definitions are provided for the sole purpose of proper interpretation and administration
of this Chapter.
APPROVED: Accepted by the American Gas Association or tests conducted by recognized technical
or scientific testing laboratories.
CERTIFICATE OF APPROVAL: A document issued and attached to the material, piping, or appliance
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 57/315
inspected, completely filled out, together with date of inspection, address of the premises or
consumer, and signed by the Inspector.
CONSUMER'S PIPING: The gas piping leading from the point of delivery to the building and the gas
appliances served.
GAS APPLIANCE: Any appliance or device used for burning natural gas or liquid petroleum gas.
GAS COMPANY: Any person holding and exercising a franchise or permit to distribute natural gas or
liquified petroleum gas within the corporate limits.
GAS COMPANY SERVICE LINE: The gas piping leading from the gas main to the point of delivery.
GAS FITTER: Any person who does any pipe fitting work, installs, repairs, or remodels any gas piping
or gas appliances.
INSPECTOR: The Building Inspector or Assistant Building Inspector, and is so designated by the
Mayor and Council of the City.
NEW GAS APPLIANCE: A gas appliance which has not been previously installed and used.
OUTLET: A threaded connection in a piping system to which a gas burning appliance is or may be
attached.
POINT OF DELIVERY: The junction of the utility's meter with the consumer's piping.
TYPE A FLUE OR VENT: A flue or vent of masonry (clay tile lined), reinforced concrete or metal
smoke stacks or approved special flues designed for gas burning equipment to accommodate flue gas
temperatures in excess of five hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit (550°F) at the draft hood.
TYPE B VENT: Vent piping of noncombustible, corrosion-resistant material of sufficient thickness and
cross-sectional area double walled, locked seam joint construction or single walled vent pipes as
approved by the National Fire Protection Association when installed in accordance with the limitations
as set forth therein.
TYPE B-W VENT: The same as type B vent but to be used with only listed vented recessed heaters.
TYPE C VENT: A vent of galvanized iron of not less than #20 U.S. Standard Gauge or of other
approved corrosion-resistant material.
USED GAS APPLIANCE: A gas appliance which has been previously installed and used.
VENT: A pipe, flue, or chimney designed and installed to carry the products of combustion from an
appliance to the outside atmosphere.
VENT OPENING: An opening or collar which is provided on a gas appliance for the purpose of
connecting the vent.
VENTED APPLIANCE: A gas appliance designed to be installed in such a manner that the products of
combustion are conveyed directly to the outside atmosphere by a vent. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-5: RESTRICTIONS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 58/315
No person shall engage in or work at the installation, extension, alteration, or repair of any gas
appliance or piping pertaining to or in connection with gas service on consumer's premises within the
corporate limits unless such person has first procured a license therefor in accordance with the
provisions of this Chapter. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-6: LICENSE REQUIRED:
A. Gas Installations: No person shall engage in the business of installing, extending, altering or
repairing any gas appliance or piping, vent or flue connection pertaining to or in connection with
gas installations within the City either as employer or individual unless such person has received a
gas installation license therefor in accordance with the provisions of this Chapter.
B. Gas Fitting Work: No person shall do any gas fitting work, install, repair or remodel any piping or
appliances which would be subject to inspection under the provisions of this Chapter unless such
person be a licensed plumber or a qualified employee of the holder of a gas installation license.
(Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-7: LICENSE NOT TRANSFERABLE:
No person shall lend his gas installation license to any other person, nor shall any such licensed
person apply for a permit in his name for use of any other person, and any such licensed person so
doing or refusing to comply with any other requirements of this Chapter shall have his gas installation
license suspended or revoked by the Mayor and Council, on the recommendation of the Board of
Examiners. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-8: APPLICATION TO DO BUSINESS:
Every person desiring to engage in the business of gas fitting or the installation of gas appliances or
gas burners of whatsoever nature in the City shall make application therefor to the Board of
Examiners and shall at such time and place as may be designated by the Board of Examiners
hereinafter provided for, to whom such application shall be referred, be examined as to his
qualifications for such business. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-9: BOARD OF EXAMINERS:
A. Membership; Term: The Board of Examiners shall consist of the representative of the Building
Inspector, Chief of the Fire Department and three (3) members to be appointed by the Mayor. One
of the appointees shall be a representative of the distributing gas company, the second shall be a
practical man engaged in gas installation, and the third, any competent person. The three (3)
appointed members shall serve for three (3) years, except for the first term, when one shall be
appointed for three (3) years, one for two (2) years and one for one year.
B. Board Of Appeals: The Board of Examiners shall also constitute the Board of Appeals. The Board
of Appeals shall meet upon call of the Inspector. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 59/315
4-5-10: EXAMINATION:
The Board of Examiners shall meet and organize by selection of a chairman and clerk and shall
designate the time and place for examination of all applicants desiring to engage in or work at the
business of installing gas appliances or gas piping in the City. Said Board shall examine said
applicants as to their practical and theoretical knowledge of gas fitting, appliance installation and
adjustment, shall submit the applicant to some satisfactory form of practical test and if satisfied of the
competency of the applicant, shall so certify to the Mayor and Council which shall authorize the Clerk
to issue a license to such applicant, authorizing him to work at the business of installing gas
appliances or gas piping, at which time he shall also cause the applicant to register in the office of the
Building Inspector, his name, place of business, residence, license number, date of examination and
to what capacity licensed. In the case of a firm or corporation, the examination of one member of the
firm or an executive of the corporation shall fulfill the requirements of this Section. The Clerk for the
Board of Examiners shall be the Building Inspector and shall be known as secretary of the Board.
(Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-11: LICENSE FEE AND BOND:
A. Annual Fee: The annual fee for the gas installation license for any firm or corporation under this
Chapter for installing gas appliances or for gas fitting shall be twenty five dollars ($25.00) per year
and the license shall be renewed on or before January 15 of each year. Said license shall continue
in force for the calendar year in which it is issued or until revoked or suspended, but shall not be
transferable.
B. Bond: Any individual engaged in the business of installing gas fixtures shall furnish a performance
bond in the sum of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), acceptable to the Council. All licenses and
bonds shall expire on January 15 of each year.
C. License Displayed: Every licensed gas installer shall display his license number conspicuously at
his place of business. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-12: LIABILITY:
This Chapter shall not be construed as relieving such persons owning, operating, installing or selling
any gas piping, appliances or other gas apparatus from liability to anyone injured by any defect
therein. Nor shall the City or any agent thereof be held as assuming any such liability by reason of the
inspection authorized hereunder or certificate of inspection issued by the Building Inspector. (Ord.
410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-13: RIGHT OF ENTRY:
The Building Inspector or his authorized representative shall have the right to enter all buildings which
contain gas piping or appliances for the purpose of inspecting same, at any reasonable time. (Ord.
410, 5-23-1967)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 60/315
4-5-14: PERMITS AND FEES:
No person shall install any gas appliance to house piping in any building or structure without first
obtaining a permit to do such work from the City. Failure to obtain a permit within forty eight (48) hours
(holidays and Sundays not included) from the time of starting work on the installation, alteration, or
repairs of any gas equipment except as otherwise provided shall pay double the fee herein specified
when such permit is finally secured. The payment of such double fee, however, shall in no way relieve
the person of the penalties otherwise provided for the violation of this Chapter.
Gas stoves $ 1.00
Gas refrigerators 1.00
Gas space heaters to 70,000 BTU input capacity 1.00
Each additional heater 0.50
Gas hot water tank, residential up to 60 gallon 1.00
Gas space heaters over 70,000 BTU input capacity 1.50
Each additional heater 1.00
Gas hot water tanks, commercial over 60 gallon 1.50
Gas boilers and furnaces up to 180,000 BTU input capacity 2.50
Gas boilers and furnaces 180,000 BTU to 400,000 BTU input capacity 4.00
Gas boilers and furnaces 400,000 BTU to 1,000,000 BTU input capacity 7.00
Gas boilers and furnaces over 1,000,000 BTU input capacity 10.00
Conversion units the same rate as above
All small appliances 1.00
Pipe Inspections:
First 50 feet or less 1.00
Each additional 50 feet or part thereof 0.50
Call back inspection, 1/2 price. Reinspection order shall be obtained from City Engineer's office.
Inspection Of Used Appliances Offered For Sale:
First appliance 1.00
Each additional appliance 0.25
When a permit is issued to connect an appliance to an existing stub or outlet, no additional fee
will be charged for piping inspection. Where new piping is required to supply the appliance, the
above fees for consumer's piping inspection will be collected.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 61/315
(Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-15: INSPECTIONS:
A. Rough Piping Inspection: Rough piping inspection shall be made after all piping authorized by the
permit has been installed, and before any such piping has been covered or concealed or any
fixtures or gas appliances have been attached thereto.
B. Test For Final Piping Inspection:
1. Test for final piping inspection shall be made after all piping authorized by the permit has been
installed and after all portions thereof which are to be concealed by plastering or otherwise have
been so concealed, and before any fixtures or gas appliances have been attached thereto. This
inspection shall include a pressure test, at which time the piping shall stand an air pressure
equal to not less than the pressure of a column of mercury six inches (6") in height, and the
piping shall hold this air pressure for a period of at least ten (10) minutes without any perceptible
drop. A U-Gauge type mercury column shall be used for the test.
2. All tools, apparatus, labor and assistance necessary for the test shall be furnished by the gas
fitter.
3. Used gas appliances for resale shall be connected to gas outlets at the time the inspection is
made.
C. Inspection Required If Structure Has Not Used Gas For Twelve Months: A new inspection
certificate shall be required for a structure in which no gas has been used for a period of twelve
(12) consecutive months or more. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-16: CERTIFICATE OF APPROVAL:
The Inspector shall issue a certificate of approval at the completion of the work for which a specific
permit has been issued, if after inspection it has been found that such work complied with the
provisions of this Chapter and all other requirements of law or ordinances applicable thereto. A
duplicate of each piping certificate shall be delivered to and filed by the gas company and used as its
authority to grant gas service. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-17: AUTHORITY AND DUTY OF INSPECTOR:
A. Enforcement; Right Of Entry: The Inspector is hereby authorized and directed to enforce all of the
provisions of this Chapter, and the Inspector or his authorized representative, upon presentation of
proper credentials, may enter any building or premises for the purpose of making inspection or
preventing violations of this Chapter at any reasonable time.
B. Authority To Disconnect; Notice: The Inspector or his authorized representative is hereby
authorized to disconnect any gas piping or fixture or appliance, which has been connected before
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 62/315
a certificate of approval has been issued, or which, upon inspection, shall be found defective or in
such condition as to endanger life or property. In all cases where such a disconnection is made, a
notice shall be affixed thereto and shall state that the same has been disconnected by the
Inspector or his representative together with the reason or reasons therefor, and it shall be
unlawful for any person to remove said notice or reconnect said gas piping or appliance until
authorized by the Inspector to do so.
C. Present Helpful Information To Council: It shall be the duty of the Inspector to confer with the
representatives of the local gas companies, of local plumbers or gas fitters associations, of the
local Health Department and the local Fire Department, and otherwise obtain from proper sources
all helpful information and advice, presenting same to the Mayor and Council from time to time for
their consideration. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-18: AUTHORITY TO DISCONNECT:
A. Issue Notice: Gas companies are hereby authorized to discontinue or refuse to supply gas for any
gas piping or gas appliance which may appear to be defective or leaking, or otherwise considered
to endanger life or property; provided, however, that the gas company shall immediately give
notice of discontinuance of service to the Inspector and the occupant of the building or premises
where such gas supply is discontinued or refused. Notice may be given by registered or certified
mail.
B. Safety Reasons: In all cases where the supply of gas has been discontinued for safety reasons, the
supplying of gas shall not be resumed until authorized by the Inspector.
C. Utility Functions: Gas companies shall not be required to secure permits to extend gas service or
set pipes or set meters or any other utility function.
D. Street Opening Permit: Gas companies shall secure street opening permits prior to installing or
extending services. Gas companies shall pay cost of opening and closing of the streets. (Ord. 410,
5-23-1967)
4-5-19: MAINTENANCE:
All gas piping, vents, vent connections, and appliances shall be maintained in good condition;
provided, however, that no gas piping, vent, vent connection, fixture, or appliance not conforming to
the requirements of this Chapter shall be used or maintained if the use or maintenance thereof would
endanger life or property, and no gas appliance shall be operated which, in the opinion of the
Inspector, is not provided with ample ventilation. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-20: VIOlATIONS; PENALTY:
A. Violations: It shall be unlawful for any person by any means to restore the flow of gas through pipes
which have been shut off either by the utility supplying the gas, or the Building Inspector. It shall be
unlawful for any person, by any means, to cause gas supplied by any utility company to bypass the
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 63/315
meter by which the amount of gas supplied by the utility company is measured and such acts shall
be prosecuted according to the terms contained in this Chapter.
B. Penalty Imposed: Any person who shall fail to comply with or who shall violate any of the provisions
of this Chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be
fined in an amount not exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00), or by imprisonment in the City jail
not exceeding thirty (30) days, or by both such fine or imprisonment. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
4-5-21: STANDARDS ADOPTED BY REFERENCE:
The following, and as the same may hereafter be amended, are hereby adopted by the City and made
a part of this Chapter by reference as though fully set forth herein:
ASA B31.8-1963: Section 8 of American Standard Code on Pressure Piping.
IENGA-1965: Inland Empire Natural Gas Association Standard for Installation of Gas Appliances and
Gas Piping, Domestic Gas Conversion Burners and Equipment in Excess of 400,000 BTU/HR Input.
NFPA No. 58: Standards of the National Board of Fire Underwriters for the Storage and Handling of
Liquefied Petroleum Gases.
NFPA No. 59: Standards of the National Board of Fire Underwriters for the Storage and Handling of
Liquefied Petroleum Gases at Utility Gas Plants.
Provided, however, that in the event the standards embodied in State and Federal laws, rules and
regulations are higher or in conflict with those contained in sources adopted by reference herein, such
standards shall control. (Ord. 410, 5-23-1967)
Chapter 6
MANUFACTURED HOUSING STANDARDS
4-6-1: SHORT TITLE:
This Chapter shall be referred to as the CITY OF OROFINO MANUFACTURED HOUSING
STANDARDS. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-2: OBJECTIVES:
The objectives of this Chapter are to provide that manufactured living units located on lots within the
City are safe, sanitary and structurally sound. The requirements contained herein shall be considered
minimum standards. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-3: DEFINITIONS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 64/315
ANCHORING SYSTEM: A system of straps, cables, turnbuckles, chains, bolts, etc., which is used to
secure a home to the foundation base.
FOUNDATION BASE: A base for support of a manufactured home meeting the requirements
contained herein.
FOUNDATION FACIA: A fire- and weather-resistant material surrounding the entire perimeter of a
home and completely enclosing the space between the exterior wall of such home and the ground.
LOT: A "building site" as defined by law.
MANUFACTURED HOME: Housing built on a chassis designed and constructed for transportation to
a site for installation and use when connected to required utilities. May also be commonly referred to
as "mobile home" or "modular home".
NONCONFORMING USE: A manufactured home which was placed and maintained upon a lot prior to
the effective date of this Chapter and which otherwise complies with this Chapter.
PERMANENTLY AFFIXED: A home which has the running gear and towing hitch removed, is
equipped with permanent foundation base and foundation facia conforming to this Chapter, and has
permanently installed connections conforming to this Code. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-4: GENERAL REQUIREMENTS:
A. Insignias: All manufactured homes shall bear a tag or a seal of approval of the State of Idaho and
HUD which shall be permanently affixed.
B. Smoke Detectors: All dwelling units shall be provided with approved detectors of combustion other
than heat, conforming to HUD standards. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-5: SITE AND DRAINAGE:
A. Compliance With Zoning Regulations: Manufactured homes shall be permanently affixed on a lot in
compliance with provisions applicable to the zones contained in the City Zoning Ordinance.
B. Surface Water Drainage; Ground Slope: The ground around the manufactured home shall be
sloped to provide positive drainage of surface water away from the foundation for a distance of ten
feet (10') unless restricted by lot line, with care being taken to avoid draining onto adjoining
property.
C. Drain Line To Storm Sewer: When the area under the manufactured home is below natural grade
level, drainage shall be provided by means of a drain line to a storm sewer, or other suitable
methods. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-6: FOUNDATION:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 65/315
A. Excavation: Except as otherwise provided in this Section, excavation for footings or foundation
walls shall extend into solid, undisturbed natural bearing soil. All vegetation and organic material
shall be removed and footings shall not be placed on fill or uncompacted gravel material unless
such fill has been compacted, and it has been certified by a licensed engineer that compaction is
sufficient to support the weight of a mobile home, as specified by the manufacturer.
B. Piers: Piers shall be set on two thousand five hundred (2,500) psi minimum concrete pads, sixteen
inches by sixteen inches by six inches (16" x 16" x 6"). All pad installation shall be pursuant to the
manufactured home standard drawings and installed at least six inches (6") into the ground so that
the exposed surface is flush with the ground. Spacing shall be eight feet (8') on center maximum.
Shims shall be required between concrete block pier and steel beam supports. Any alternate
design shall be supported by engineering calculations. (Ord. 608, 12-10-1985)
1. Piers comprised of a single tier of open cell concrete blocks must be placed with cells in a
vertical position. The height between ground level and the mobile home floor joists shall be at
least eighteen inches (18") and cannot exceed the height of twenty four inches (24"). The blocks
must be installed at right angles to the steel chassis beam.
2. Any pier height over twenty four inches (24") must be double-tiered and interlocked. In no case
can this type of support system exceed seventy two inches (72") nor shall more than twenty
percent (20%) of the total number of piers exceed forty inches (40") in height. The top blocks are
to be installed at right angles to the steel beams.
3. All piers exceeding seventy two inches (72") in height require a variance. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-7: ANCHORING:
Tie down devices must be approved by the Building Official and shall be installed as to secure home
to foundation footing: tie down loops in footing, a system of straps, cables, turnbuckles, chains, bolts,
etc. Tie down straps shall be installed a minimum of five feet (5') from each corner and thereafter at
intervals not to exceed sixteen feet (16') around the complete perimeter of the home. (Ord. 603, 9-24-
1985)
4-6-8: SKIRTING:
A. Foundation Facia: The space between the wall of the home and the ground shall be fully enclosed
with a foundation facia which is aesthetically harmonious and compatible with the home, must
provide adequate ventilation and access and must be properly maintained.
1. Access Door: Access door shall be at least eighteen inches by twenty four inches (18" x 24") in
size.
2. Ventilation Openings: Ventilation openings must be provided for each twenty five (25) lineal feet
of skirting and within two feet (2') of each corner. Each opening shall have a minimum net area
of thirty six (36) square inches and must have a corrosion-resistant wire mesh not less than onefourth
inch (1/4") nor more than one-half inch (1/2") in any dimension.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 66/315
B. Pressure-Treated Wood: Wood in contact with the ground is not acceptable unless wood is
pressure-treated and bears a stamp identifying the materials as pressure-treated for ground
contact.
C. Wood Skirting Support Members: Wood skirting support members must be pressure-treated or
have a minimum of six inches (6") of clearance by use of a metal end clamp. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-9: AWNINGS:
A. Metal Awnings And Carports: Metal awning and carports must be approved and be installed in an
approved manner and meet all design loads for the City.
B. Site-Built Awnings: Site-built awnings must be UBC minimum standards. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-10: PORCHES AND ENTRY PLATFORMS:
A. Entry Platform Or Porch Floor: The main entry platform or porch floor shall be at least forty eight
inches by forty eight inches (48" x 48").
B. Handrails; Guardrails; Decks: When the floor of the platform or porch exceeds a height of four (4) or
more risers, a handrail and guardrail must be provided on open sides of the porch deck.
1. Guardrails for platforms and decks shall be no less than thirty six inches (36") in height,
constructed of durable materials and have adequate strength for the intended purpose.
2. Stair handrails shall be from thirty inches (30") to thirty four inches (34") above the front edge of
each stop.
3. Decks constructed of wood, platforms, or porches shall be supported on concrete blocks or slab
with a minimum of four inch (4") separation between wood and ground surface.
C. Service Entries: Service entries four (4) steps or higher or served by doors swinging outward shall
have porch floors, steps and handrails conforming to the main entry requirements.
D. Step Designs: The following shall be required for stairs serving main and service entrance doors:
1. Width, that of walk but not less than thirty inches (30").
2. Run, minimum of nine inches (9").
3. Rise, maximum eight inches (8"). All riser heights shall be the same.
4. Provide handrails continuous on all open sides of stair flights to a platform with four (4) or more
risers.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 67/315
E. Compliance: All porch and entry platforms must comply with the City manufactured home standard
drawings. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-11: WATER SUPPLY AND SANITATION:
All units shall be connected to an approved water and sewer system in accordance with City
standards. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-12: FIREPLACES; STOVES:
A. Conformance With Section: Solid fuel-burning factory-built fireplaces, wood heaters and fireplace
stoves UL or ICBO approved for use in mobile homes may be installed in mobile homes, provided
the units and their installation conform to this Section. A fireplace or fireplace stove shall not be
considered as the primary heating facility.
B. Installation Requirements: A solid fuel-burning fireplace or fireplace stove shall be equipped with
integral door(s) or shutter(s) designed to close the fireplace or fireplace stove fire chamber opening
and shall include complete means for venting through the roof, a combustion air inlet, a hearth
extension, and means to securely attach the fireplace or the fireplace stove to the mobile home
structure. The installation shall conform to the following:
1. A listed factory-built chimney designed to be attached directly to fireplace or fireplace stove shall
be used. The listed factory-built chimney shall be equipped with and contain as part of its listing
a termination device(s) and a spark arrester.
2. A fireplace or fireplace stove, air intake assembly, hearth extension and the chimney shall be
installed in accordance with the terms of their listings and their manufacturer's instructions.
3. The combustion air inlet shall conduct air directly into the fire chamber and shall be designed to
prevent material from the hearth dropping into the area beneath the mobile home.
4. Hearth extension shall be of noncombustible material not less than three-eighths inch (3/8")
thick. The hearth shall extend at least sixteen inches (16") in front of and at least eight inches
(8") beyond each side of the fireplace or fireplace stove opening. Furthermore, the hearth shall
extend over the entire surface beneath a fireplace stove and beneath and elevated for an
overhanging fireplace.
5. The label on each solid fuel-burning fireplace and solid fuel-burning fireplace stove shall include
the following wording: "For use with solid fuel only" and shall indicate ICBO or UL approved.
6. The chimney shall extend at least three feet (3') above the part of the roof through which it
passes and at least two feet (2') above the highest elevation of any part of the mobile home
within ten feet (10') of the chimney. Portions of the chimney and termination that exceed an
elevation of thirteen feet (13') above ground level may be designed to be removed for
transporting the home. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-13: ALTERATIONS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 68/315
A permit from the State is required for alterations for any mechanical, electrical, plumbing system for a
structural change. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
4-6-14: SITE PERMIT; INFORMATION REQUIRED:
A site permit shall be acquired from the Building Official prior to occupancy. The following information
shall be included in the site permit application:
A. Show lot and block number, street address if known.
B. Show dimensions of plat and north arrow.
C. Show locations and dimensions of mobile home, floor plan, setback requirements, easements if
any, awnings, carports, garages, and other accessory buildings.
D. Show location and dimension of walks, driveway and approach steps, patios and porches.
E. Show easements off-site to public right of way and nonbenefiting easement to adjoining properties.
F. Show water and sewer site schematics.
G. Show the nature and type of skirting.
H. Show foundation and placement permit.
I. Show septic tank permit (if manufactured home is not connected to an approved sewer). (Ord. 603,
9-24-1985)
4-6-15: PERMIT FEES:
Fees for permits will be established by Council action. (Ord. 603, 9-24-1985)
Chapter 7
MECHANICAL CODE
4-7-1: ADOPTION:
The 2003 international mechanical code is hereby adopted along with all future editions and
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 69/315
amendments establishing minimum regulations governing the design, construction, quality of
materials, erection, installation, alteration, repair, location, relocation, replacement, addition to, use or
maintenance of mechanical systems as herein provided; providing for the issuance of permits and
collection of fees therefor; and each and all of the regulations, provisions, penalties, conditions and
terms of said mechanical code on file in the office of the city clerk are hereby referred to, adopted, and
made a part hereof, as if fully set out in this chapter, with the additions, insertions, deletions and
changes, if any, prescribed in section 4-7-2 of this chapter. (Ord. 727, 8-22-2005, eff. 10-1-2005)
4-7-2: AMENDMENTS:
The following sections are hereby revised:
Section 101.1 Title: These regulations shall be known as the Mechanical Code Of The City Of
Orofino, hereinafter referred to as "this code."
Section 106.5.2 Fee Schedule: The fee for a mechanical inspection shall be $35.00.
Section 106.5.3 Fee Refunds: This section is hereby deleted from the international mechanical code.
Section 108.4 Violation Penalties: Persons who shall violate a provision of this code or shall fail to
comply with any of the requirements thereof or who shall erect, install, alter or repair mechanical work
in violation of the approved construction documents or directive of the code official, or of a permit or
certificate issued under the provisions of this code, shall be punishable by a fine of not more than
$300.00 or by imprisonment not exceeding thirty (30) days, or both such fine and imprisonment. Each
day that a violation continues after due notice has been served shall be deemed a separate offense.
Section 108.5 Stop Work Orders: Upon notice from the official code that mechanical work is being
done contrary to the provisions of this code or in a dangerous or unsafe manner, such work shall
immediately cease. Such notice shall be in writing and shall be given to the owner of the property, or
to the owner's agent, or to the person doing the work. The notice shall state the conditions under
which work is authorized to resume. Where an emergency exists, the code official shall not be
required to give a written notice prior to stopping the work. Any person who shall continue any work on
the system after having been served with a stop work order, except such work as that person is
directed to perform to remove a violation or unsafe condition, shall be liable for a fine not less than
$300.00.
(Ord. 727, 8-22-2005, eff. 10-1-2005)
Chapter 8
CONTRACTOR REGISTRATION
4-8-1: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter shall be referred to as the IDAHO CONTRACTORS REGISTRATION ACT. (Ord. 730, 1-
10-2006)
4-8-2: CONTRACTORS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 70/315
All contractors who perform work in excess of two thousand dollars ($2,000.00) (material and labor)
within the city limits of the city of Orofino shall be required to register with the Idaho bureau of
occupational licenses (IBOL) and provide a registration number to the building official prior to receiving
a permit to perform any work. (Ord. 730, 1-10-2006)
4-8-3: EXEMPTIONS:
Contractors who are exempt from registration pursuant to Idaho Code 54, chapter 52 shall not be
required to register with the Idaho bureau of occupational licenses (IBOL). (Ord. 730, 1-10-2006)
4-8-4: DUTIES OF BUILDING OFFICIAL:
The building official or his representative shall not issue a building or construction permit to
contractors who are not registered with the Idaho bureau of occupational licenses by January 1, 2006.
The building official shall conspicuously enter the contractor's registration number on the face of any
permit issued. If a contractor or individual is exempt from registration, the building official shall
conspicuously enter on the face of any permit issued "No Contractor Registration Provided". (Ord.
730, 1-10-2006)
4-8-5: PERMITS TO BE POSTED:
All building permits or other permits for construction of any type shall be posted at the construction site
in such a manner that the conspicuous statements set forth in section 4-8-4 of this chapter are visible.
(Ord. 730, 1-10-2006)
Title 5
BUSINESS REGULATIONS
Chapter 1
BUSINESS PERMITS
5-1-1: STATUTORY AUTHORITY; PURPOSE:
The licensing of all retail occupations and businesses within the city and the levying of a permit fee,
uniform to all classes imposed, pursuant to the statutory authority vested in the city by Idaho Code
section 50-307 is hereby declared to be justified and necessary for the purpose of protecting and
providing services to the citizens of the city and the businesses and occupations doing business
therein. (Ord. 784, 5-12-2015)
5-1-2: DEFINITIONS:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 71/315
For the purposes of this chapter, the following words shall have the meanings indicated, unless the
context clearly requires otherwise:
BUILDING: A structure completely enclosed by walls and covered by a roof which is permanently
affixed to a foundation and permanently attached to water and sewer utility services.
BUSINESS OR OCCUPATION: All activities, occupations, callings, trades, pursuits or professions
located or engaged in within the city with the object of gain, profit, benefit or advantage. Each
business location shall be deemed to be a separate business, unless it is a specific annex to the main
location of the business.
CANVASSER OR SOLICITOR: Any individual, whether resident of the city or not, either traveling by
foot, wagon, automobile, motor truck or any other type of conveyance, from place to place, from house
to house, or from street to street, taking or attempting to take orders for the sale of goods, wares and
merchandise, personal property or personal services of any nature whatsoever for future delivery, or
for services to be furnished or performed in the future, whether or not such individual has, carries or
exposes for sale a sample of the subject of such sale or whether he is collecting advance payments
on such sales or not.
EMPLOYEE: Any person employed at any business location within the city and any person furnishing
or performing services within the city. It shall include all persons who are self-employed and shall
include part time employees.
ENGAGING IN BUSINESS: Commencing, conducting or continuing any business or occupation, the
exercise of corporate and franchise powers and the liquidating of a business where the liquidators
hold themselves out to the public as conducting such business. Any person shall be deemed to be
engaging in doing business when s/he does one act of the following:
A. Selling any goods or performing any services;
B. Soliciting business or offering or holding out goods or services for sale or hire;
C. Acquiring or using any vehicle or any premises in the city for business purposes;
D. Delivery of any goods for the purpose of retail unless permitted under another section of this
code.
HOME OCCUPATION1: Any occupation by one member of the family without employees and located
in one or two (2) rooms of a home or its accessory buildings and without storage of materials or stock
of finished products for sale on the premises. A home occupation shall not detract from or change the
integrity or character of the residential zone. There shall not be any outside indication such as signage
or other indication that a home occupation exists at a residence.
MOBILE VENDING CART: A movable pushcart that is operated by a vendor standing on the sidewalk.
MOBILE VENDING TRAILER: A mobile trailer operated by a vendor standing on or within the frame of
the trailer on the public rights of way between the curbs.
MOBILE VENDING VEHICLE: Motorized vehicle operated by a vendor standing on or within the frame
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 72/315
of the vehicle on the public rights of way between the curb lines.
