8-2-28: SYSTEM OF CHARGES:
All systems of charges and fees to users within and without the City service area shall assure that
each recipient of wastewater collection and treatment services will pay its proportionate share of the
costs of operation and maintenance (including equipment replacement) of any waste collection and
treatment services provided by the City. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-29: SEWER CONNECTION FEES:
Before any sewer connection permit is issued for the installation of any sewer service connection (side
sewer), the person making the application therefor shall pay to the City both an "equity buy in" fee and
a sewer connection charge as herein set forth:
A. Equity Buy In Fees: An "equity buy in" fee shall be paid for each connection made to the sewer
system, for wastewater collection lines and for wastewater treatment plant based on water meter
hook-up size, in accordance with the following schedule:

B. Connection And Inspection Charge: A connection and inspection charge shall be paid for each

mains were installed by local improvement district assessment, in accordance with the following
schedule:
1. Single-family dwelling or unit, each sewer connection: Three hundred dollars ($300.00).
2. Multifacility dwelling or unit, each sewer connection: Three hundred dollars ($300.00), plus the
following:
a. Mobile home courts or mobile subdivisions: Three hundred dollars ($300.00) per each trailer
space in excess of one.
b. Motels, motor hotels, cabin courts, travel trailer courts: Thirty dollars ($30.00) per room, cabin
or trailer space.
c. Apartment houses, duplexes and similar multiple living units (for each building): Two hundred
dollars ($200.00) per living unit in excess of one.
d. Condominiums and townhouses: Three hundred dollars ($300.00) per living unit in excess of
one.
e. Commercial buildings and others not specifically covered above: Ten dollars ($10.00) per
plumbing fixture in excess of six (6) per premises.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 190/315
f. Industrial facilities: As may be established by the city council.
C. When Payment Required: All "equity buy in" and service connection charges shall be paid at the
time the service connection is requested.
D. Failure To Pay: Failure to pay the connection and inspection charge shall result in a
connection/inspection charge of two (2) times the regular charge and may result in a nonissuance
by the city of the occupancy permit.
E. Exceptions: The above "equity buy in" fees and sewer connection charge will not apply to or be
charged against the reconstruction of any existing sewer service line serving any existing dwelling,
building, etc. It is intended that both the "equity buy in" fee and a sewer connection charge be
charged only where a new building is being constructed upon previously undeveloped property.
These fees may be changed from time to time, by resolution of the city council, as such charges
are deemed necessary. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-30: SERVICE CALL CHARGE:
The superintendent may require a service charge in an amount not to exceed the actual cost to the
city for service calls which are only for the convenience and benefit of the customer. (Ord. 655, 9-27-
1994)
8-2-31: FLOW CHARGE VARIATIONS:
The monthly flow charge for residential sewer charges shall be the average water usage (metered
water) for the months of November, December, January and February. This average shall be used to
calculate sewer flow charges throughout the twelve (12) months of the year and shall be recalculated
each year for a new average. Households who have not established a true winter average for the four
(4) months mentioned above shall be assigned an average based on the number of individuals who
reside in the house. This average shall be computed at fifty (50) gallons of metered water per day per
individual. Commercial businesses will be based upon actual water usage (metered water). (Res. 337,
5-10-2004, eff. retroactive to 5-1-2004)
8-2-32: MONTHLY SCHEDULE OF RATES:
A sewer charge shall be levied on all users of the sewage collection and treatment facilities to cover
the actual or estimated cost of operation, maintenance, replacement and financing of the facilities. The
user charge system shall distribute these costs to each user or user class in approximate portion to
such user's contribution to the total wastewater load of such facilities as follows:
A. Single-Family And/Or Commercial Units: Owners of a "single-family" and/or "commercial unit", as
defined in section 8-2-2 of this chapter, shall pay monthly the basic rate plus the usage rate per
gallon, as set by resolution, and as determined by metered water usage.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 191/315
B. Multifacility Units: Owners of "multifacility units", as defined in section 8-2-2 of this chapter, shall
pay monthly the basic rate for one facility and two-thirds (2/3) of the basic rate for each additional
facility, plus the usage rate based upon metered water.
C. Single-Family Unit Or Commercial Unit Not Receiving Metered Water: Owners of a single-family
unit and/or commercial unit, not receiving metered water from the city, shall pay a monthly basic
rate as set by resolution. In addition to the basic rate, owners of the commercial unit may be
required to install an approved flow monitoring device, or the city may establish a user charge rate
based upon an equivalent user schedule.
D. Multifacility Units Not Receiving Metered Water Service: Owners of multifacility units, not receiving
metered water service from the city, shall pay the monthly basic rate as set by resolution for each
facility.
E. High Strength Users: For high strength users, wastewater loading contributions will be based upon
the same flow charge per unit volume plus a surcharge on excess BOD and SS based upon
industrial recovery requirements as set forth in 40 CFR 35.925-11, 35.925-12, 35.935-13 and
35.928.
F. Notification Of Change In Rates: The council shall review the sewer use rate biannually and based
upon the actual costs of operation, maintenance, replacement and financing of wastewater
collection and treatment services, shall revise the sewer use rates accordingly. The city shall notify
each user of any changes in the sewer use charges attributable to the collection and treatment
services. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-33: METER SERVICE:
Whenever the council deems it appropriate and in the best interest of the city and its citizens to
require a user to have the sewer service to his or her facilities metered to more appropriately
determine the amount of service provided such user by the system, the council may, by resolution,
require the said user to install a meter and/or meters which will accurately measure the service
provided. And the council may further establish by resolution the rates to be charged for such service
as will properly pay the fair share of the services provided such user. The cost of the meter and its
installation shall be borne by the user. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-34: DELINQUENT ACCOUNTS; DISCONTINUANCE AND RESTORATION FEE:
When bills are not paid within thirty (30) days from the past due date, the superintendent shall issue
an order to shut off and discontinue water service to such delinquent customers. In case service is
discontinued for delinquency, it shall not be restored until the delinquency is paid, or until
arrangements for payment satisfactory to the city clerk have been made, together with a fee of ten
dollars ($10.00) for discontinuing and restoring service. The fee of ten dollars ($10.00) shall be
payable whenever a service trip is made for the purpose of discontinuing service because of
nonpayment, even though an actual shutoff may not actually have occurred. In the event that a
delinquent customer fails to pay his or her bill within the time set forth above, the city may discontinue
city water service or remove or close sewer connections, and enter upon the property for
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 192/315
accomplishing such purposes. The expense of digging up and plugging the sewer service line, as well
as the expense of restoring said sewer service line back to an operable condition is a debt due to the
city and may be recovered by legal action against the sewer user, in addition to the ten dollar ($10.00)
fee set forth above. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-35: SEWER SYSTEM MATERIALS AND INSTALLATIONS:
A. Compliance: All sanitary sewer main line and storm drain main line materials, manholes, etc., and
their installation shall be in accordance with city standard specifications for the construction of
sanitary sewers and storm sewers and the applicable standard drawings depicting various sewer
line installation details.
B. Acceptable Materials: All sewer system materials shall be of the class, strength, thickness, etc.,
necessary to accommodate or provide for the depth of cover over the pipe, the type of material and
bedding around the pipe, and the type, magnitude and extent of the external loads being applied to
the pipe.
C. Approval By City: All materials must be approved by the City. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-36: SEWER SYSTEM DESIGN:
A. Plans: The plans for all sewer lines, sewage lift stations, sewage treatment facilities, etc., shall be
designed, signed and sealed by a registered professional engineer licensed in the State, as the
City deems necessary.
B. State Health Department Requirements: All sewer lines, lift stations, sewage treatment facilities,
etc., shall be designed and approved in accordance with State Health Department requirements.
C. Minimum Size: Minimum sanitary main size shall be eight inch (8") diameter, unless a special
design is approved by the City where the sewer line may be reduced. Minimum storm drain size
shall be eight inches (8") in diameter. Larger sizes shall be required by the City's overall sewer
system master plan or as needed to provide adequate sewage-carrying capacity for the area (and
surrounding developable area) being developed and/or annexed to the City. Minimum building
service line (side sewer) size shall be four inches (4") in diameter.
D. Generally: In general, sewers shall be sufficiently deep so as to receive sewage from basements
and to prevent freezing. Sewer lines shall have at least three feet (3') of cover (from the top of the
sewer line pipe to the ground or street surface) unless a special design is approved by the City
whereby the sewer line is protected from freezing by special means or methods and the sewer is
protected from "heaving" by installation of crushed gravel backfill material under, around and over
the pipe.
E. Design And Construction: All sewer mains shall be designed and constructed to provide mean
velocities, when flowing full of not less than two feet (2') per second. All sewer service lines (side
sewers) shall be designed and constructed to provide mean velocities, when flowing full, of not
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 193/315
less than three feet (3') per second. The following are minimum slopes which should be provided;
however, slopes greater than these are desirable:
Sewer Size
Minimum Slope In Feet
Per 100 Feet
4 inch 2.00
6 inch 1.00
8 inch 0.40
10 inch 0.28
12 inch 0.22
15 inch 0.15
18 inch 0.12
21 inch 0.10
24 inch 0.08
27 inch 0.067
30 inch 0.058
36 inch 0.046
Under special conditions, if detailed justifiable reasons are given, slopes slightly less than those
required above (i.e., to provide 2.0 or 3.0 fsp velocity when flowing full) may be permitted. Such
decreased slopes will only be considered where the depth of flow will be 0.3 of the diameter or
greater for the design average flow. Whenever such decreased slopes are proposed, the design
engineer must furnish with his or her report his or her computations of the depths of flow, in such
pipes at the minimum and average rates of flow for a typical day.
Sewers shall be laid with uniform slopes between manholes (i.e., a manhole shall be constructed
at each point where the sewer line slope or grade changes).
F. Manholes: Manholes shall be located no more than four hundred feet (400') apart on lines fifteen
inches (15") in diameter or smaller. Manholes may be located up to six hundred feet (600') apart on
lines larger than fifteen inches (15") in diameter. Manholes shall be installed at all locations where
sewer lines eight inches (8") in diameter or larger intersect, join together or make a bend. All deadend
sewer lines shall have a manhole installed on the end thereof or a lamp well where approved
by the Superintendent.
G. Sewer Mainline Drop Through Manholes: The flow line of the main sewer line as it enters and
leaves any manhole shall be dropped as follows:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 194/315
Mainline Bend Of Drop Of
0 - 10 degrees Regular pipe slope
10 - 45 degrees 0.05 feet
45 - 90 degrees 0.10 feet
H. Lateral Sewer Line Connections At Manholes: Lateral sanitary sewer lines shall not enter a
manhole at an elevation appreciably higher than the sewer mainline. The flow line(s) of any lateral
line(s) shall be positioned within the manhole as follows:
1. The flow line of the main sewer line shall be at least 0.05 foot below the flow line on any of the
lateral sewer lines entering the manhole.
2. Where the diameter of the main line and the lateral line differ by less than 0.5 foot, the top of the
lateral line shall be positioned even with the top of the main line on its highest (inlet) side.
3. Where the diameter of the main and lateral differ by 0.5 foot or more, the two (2) sewer line
inverts shall be positioned at the same elevation.
4. Where a lateral sewer line would enter a manhole at an elevation of three feet (3') or more
above the main sewer line, "drop manhole" construction shall be utilized to locate or position the
flow line of the lateral line (in relation to that of the main line) as indicated above.
5. Where a lateral line would enter a manhole at an elevation of less than three feet (3') above the
main sewer line, the grade or slope of the lateral shall be adjusted so that its flow line is located
(in relation to that of the main line) as indicated above.
Individual building service lines may not enter manholes; except that no more than two (2)
individual building service lines may enter a "dead-end" manhole (a manhole on the upstream
and permanent end of a sewer line); and provided further, that the individual building service
lines must enter the manhole at such elevation that the top of the service line is level with the top
of the sewer main line and that the poured-in-place concrete floor of the manhole brings the flow
lines of the service lines into the flow line of the main line in a smooth continuous manner.
I. Location Of Sewer And Water Lines: Sanitary sewer lines and water lines shall, wherever possible,
be located on opposite sides of the street, a ten foot (10') (out-to-out) horizontal separation
between water line facilities and sewer line facilities (either sanitary or storm) and an eighteen inch
(18") (out-to-out) vertical separation between said line facilities shall always be maintained, unless
a specific variance to this requirement is obtained from the City. The applicable separation
requirements of the Idaho Health Department shall also be complied with.
J. Drawings: All drawings shall be on linen or mylar in pencil or ink and of such quality that they clearly
show the dimensions, location, sizes, etc., of all facilities represented thereon. All sewer line
manholes, inlet boxes, building service lines, etc., shall be clearly shown and identified by name
and station or other means of horizontal location. Sewer lines shall be shown both plan and profile
unless the length of said sewer line or sewer line extension is so short that the City waives this
requirement. If a profile of the sewer line is not provided, it shall be located in the vertical plane by
elevations on the flow line of the pipe at all manholes, inlet boxes, etc., and at other such locations
and intervals as the City may require. Drawings shall be drawn on a scale of one inch equals one
hundred feet (1" = 100') unless the amount of detail, topography, etc., necessitates their being
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 195/315
drawn on a larger scale (i.e., 1" = 40') to provide the clarity and completeness needed on the
drawings.
K. Approval Of City: The design of all sewer lines and all sewer system plans must be approved by the
City. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-37: AS-BUILT DRAWINGS AND ENGINEER'S CERTIFICATION:
A. As-Built Or Record Drawings: As-built or record drawings of sewer line plans shall be prepared by a
professional engineer and the "corrected" original drawing or a duplicate mylar copy of the
"corrected" original drawing(s) shall be provided to the City.
B. Certification Required: As-built plans shall include a certification thereon signed by the registered
professional engineer in charge of the work that the as-built drawings are true and correct and that
he/she (the registered professional engineer) has inspected the construction of the sewer line
installation and that the materials and installation of same were all done in conformity with the
standard specifications for the construction of sanitary sewers and storm sewers. (Ord. 655, 9-27-
1994)
8-2-38: RESPONSIBILITY FOR SEWER LINES:
A. Construction Of Sewer Line: The owner or developer of any piece of property or tract of land is
responsible for the construction of the sewer line (or for the sewer line costs) along any property
sides or frontages of the property along which a sewer line is needed for the overall completeness
and continuity of the city's sewer main system. If it is a large tract of land, the owner or developer
shall also be responsible for the necessary and required system of sewer lines within the interior of
the tract of land. The owner or developer of any piece of property shall construct all needed sewer
lines of the approved size within and along all sides or frontages of any piece of property prior to
the time any building construction thereon is occupied or utilized unless "phased" construction of
the sewer main system is specifically allowed or provided for in the annexation or development
agreement.
B. Costs: The owner or developer of any property or subdivision will normally be responsible only for
the cost of up to an eight inch (8") diameter sanitary sewer line. The additional cost of providing a
sanitary sewer line of a size greater than eight inches (8") will normally be a city responsibility. The
city will reimburse the developer for the extra cost of the additional sanitary sewer line size (over
the 8 inch diameter size referenced above) as set forth in the annexation or development
agreement between the developer and the city. Provided further, however, that if any proposed
subdivision or development is of such size or magnitude that it requires or necessitates a sewer
size larger than an eight inch (8") diameter line or if the type of development is such as to produce
a wastewater flow in excess of the capacity of an eight inch (8") diameter sewer line, then the
owner or developer of said subdivision shall be responsible for the entire cost to whatever size of
sewer line is needed to accommodate his or her development. The additional cost of providing any
extra sewer line depth required by the city (over and above the sewer line depth required to
adequately serve the owner or developer's property when assuming at least a 12 foot sewer line
depth at the uppermost end of the sewer line extended through or along said property) will be a
city responsibility and the city will reimburse the owner or developer for the cost of said extra depth
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 196/315
of sewer line as agreed upon and as set forth in the annexation or development agreement
between the developer and the city. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-39: RESPONSIBILITY FOR SEWAGE LIFT STATIONS:
Sewer mains shall be kept as deep as practicable to keep sewage lift stations to the smallest number
possible. When a sewage lift station and its related facilities is required, it and the sewer main system
to which it is directing sewage, shall generally be designed for an entire definable area and not just to
serve a single property owner or developer. The cost of the sewage lift station shall be equitably
divided between the developer and the city as set forth in the annexation or development agreement.
(Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-40: CITATION ISSUANCE; APPEARANCE REQUIRED:
Whenever it is determined by any police officer or other duly authorized officer that any person or
persons have violated any provisions of this chapter, the said officer shall provide in quadruplicate and
serve upon such person or persons a written citation containing a notice to appear in a designated
court of competent jurisdiction within the city. This citation shall contain the name and address of the
person charged, the offense charged, the time and place when and where the offense charged
occurred, and the time when the person charged shall appear in said court, and such other pertinent
information as may be necessary; and such person or persons shall appear in said court within five (5)
days after such citation is issued and served. The issuance of a citation shall not be the exclusive
method of summoning offenders hereunder. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-41: FAILURE TO APPEAR:
It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to fail or neglect to appear in response to and as
required by the citation regardless of the disposition of the charge upon which such citation was
originally issued. Appearance in court shall be deemed complied with upon appearance by the person
cited or his or her attorney. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-42: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction thereof, may be punished by a fine of not more than three hundred dollars ($300.00) or by
imprisonment for not more than thirty (30) days or both such fine and imprisonment. Each day said
violation occurs shall be a separate offense. (Ord. 655, 9-27-1994)
8-2-43: AMENDMENT OF SEWER RATES, FEES SCHEDULES AND CHARGES:
The monthly schedule of rates, connection fees, system charges, equity buy in fees, and any other
rates or fees identified in this chapter shall be amended by resolution. All other sections of this chapter
shall be amended by ordinance. (Ord. 721, 5-10-2004)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 197/315
Title 9
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
Chapter 1
SIDEWALKS
9-1-1: SPECIFICATIONS:
The material and method of constructing sidewalks shall conform in all respects to the specifications
adopted by the City Council. These specifications shall be on file in the Clerk's office at all times.
(1962 Code)
9-1-2: PROPERTY OWNER MUST CONSTRUCT SIDEWALKS:
It shall be the duty of every property owner, upon notification by the City Council, to construct or repair
sidewalks as such is prescribed in said notice. (1962 Code)
9-1-3: FAILURE TO COMPLY:
If such property owner shall fail, after notification, to construct or repair any sidewalk, the City Council
may order same constructed or repaired. The costs of said work shall be assessed against the
property owner for which said sidewalk was constructed or repaired and said cost shall become a lien
upon the property. (1962 Code)
Chapter 2
REMOVAL OF SNOW AND/OR ICE
9-2-1: REMOVAL REQUIRED:
It shall be the duty of the owner or tenant of any premises abutting or adjoining any public sidewalk to
remove all snow and/or ice from such sidewalk. (1962 Code)
9-2-2: NOTICE TO BE GIVEN:
It shall be the duty of the City to give notice to any owner or tenant of any property to remove snow
and/or ice, which notice shall be sent by registered mail to the last known address of such owner,
tenant or occupant. The owner or occupant shall have not more than twenty four (24) hours from and
after receipt of such notice, within which to remove the snow and/or ice as set forth in said notice.
(1962 Code)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 198/315
9-2-3: FAILURE TO COMPLY, CITY TO REMOVE:
Upon failure of an owner or tenant to comply with the provisions of this Chapter, the City shall have
the right to remove such snow and/or ice and assess the cost thereof against the premises abutting
the sidewalk. Such assessment shall be certified to the County Assessor or other proper County
official having charge of the making of the assessment roll and such charge shall be placed on the
assessment roll and collected in the same manner as other City taxes are collected. (1962 Code)
Chapter 3
TREES
9-3-1: TITLE:
This Chapter shall be known as the OROFINO TREE ORDINANCE. (Ord. 674, 1-12-1998)
9-3-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this Chapter is to establish and maintain an optimum amount, species variety and age
diversity of tree cover on public lands in the City and to maintain City trees in a healthy and minimally
hazardous condition through good arboricultural practices. (Ord. 674, 1-12-1998)
9-3-3: DEFINITIONS:
ADMINISTRATOR: The individual or individuals, as appointed and overseen by the terms of this
Chapter.
DEVELOPMENT: The alteration, construction or implementation of any building, structure, or use on
any piece of property or within any right of way.
PUBLIC PROPERTY: Property owned by the City of Orofino either in fee simple absolute, or implied
or expressly dedicated to the public for present or future use, for purposes of vehicular or pedestrian
traffic, or for public easements.
PUBLIC TREE: Any tree, shrub, or other woody vegetation on public property.
SHRUB: A multiple stemmed, woody plant whose height at maturity is between three feet (3') and
fifteen feet (15').
STREET TREE: Any tree, shrub or other woody vegetation on lands within any City right of way.
TREE: A woody perennial plant with one main stem or trunk. (Ord. 674, 1-12-1998)
9-3-4: URBAN FORESTS OF OROFINO COMMITTEE:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 199/315
A. Committee Created; Membership: There is hereby created and established a City Tree Board to be
known as "Urban Forests of Orofino" for the City, which shall consist of seven (7) members,
citizens and residents of this community, who shall be appointed by the Mayor with the approval of
the City Council.
B. Term Of Office: The term of the seven (7) persons to be appointed by the Mayor shall be three (3)
years except that the term of two (2) of the members appointed to the first Board shall be for only
one year and the term of two (2) members of the first Board shall be for two (2) years. In the event
that a vacancy shall occur during the term of any member, his successor shall be appointed for the
unexpired portion of the term.
C. Compensation: Members of the Board shall serve without compensation.
D. Duties And Responsibilities:
1. It shall be the responsibility of the Board to study, investigate, counsel and develop and/or
update a written plan for the care, preservation, pruning, planting, replanting, removal or
disposition of trees and shrubs in public ways, streets and alleys. Such plan will be presented to
the City Council and upon their acceptance and approval shall constitute the Official
Comprehensive City Tree Plan for the City.
2. The Board, when requested by the City Council, shall consider, investigate, make findings,
report and recommend upon any special matter of question coming within the scope of its work.
E. Operation: The Board shall choose its own officers, make its own rules and regulations and keep a
record of its proceedings. A majority of the members shall be a quorum for the transaction of
business. (Ord. 674, 1-12-1998)
9-3-5: PUBLIC TREES:
A. Street Trees: All development, with the exception of the construction of single-family homes or
duplexes, shall include planting of street trees in accordance with the Plan or as required by the
Orofino Planning and Zoning Commission. Developers shall assume the cost of the purchase,
planting, irrigation, maintenance, and replacement of all street trees within any development. The
length of term of that responsibility shall not be less than three (3) years. Developers may provide
surety, in the same form and under the same specifications as for all other infrastructure, for the
installation of trees.
B. Violation: It shall be a violation of this Chapter for any person to abuse, destroy, poison, or mutilate
any public tree, plant or shrub, or the root of any public tree, plant or shrub. It shall be a violation of
this Chapter to top any public tree.
C. Permit Required: Permits shall be required for property owners to remove, prune or plant any street
tree. Permits for removal shall be issued only if the property owner has established, to the
administrator's satisfaction, that there is need for the removal.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 200/315
D. Owners Of Adjacent Property: Owners of property adjacent to a street tree shall provide adequate
maintenance for that tree. Adequate maintenance shall include sufficient water, proper pruning,
supportive staking if needed, and protection from compaction or injury by vehicles or other causes.
E. Proper Care And Maintenance: The administrator shall encourage the proper care and
maintenance of public trees through the education of public utilities, tree removal and maintenance
companies, and private citizens.
F. Removal Of Trees: The administrator shall remove or cause the removal of public or private trees or
branches which provide a hazard to the public health, safety or welfare, or public trees which
should be removed to further sound community forestry goals.
G. Disease Or Pest In Trees: Upon the discovery of an epidemic disease or pest in any public or
private tree, the administrator shall serve notice upon the owner of the tree which shall require that
owner to eradicate, remove, or otherwise control such conditions within a given time frame.
H. Variance Required: A variance shall be required when a property owner wants to deviate from the
rules and regulations of this Chapter. (Ord. 674, 1-12-1998)
9-3-6: ENFORCEMENT:
Any person violating any provisions of this Chapter shall be punished by a fine equal to or less than
the monetary value of the tree as assessed by the administrator. The administrator shall use the tree
value assessment guidelines established by the International Society of Arboricultural Specialists, and
the amount of damage to the tree, in assessing fines. (Ord. 674, 1-12-1998)
Chapter 4
NOXIOUS WEEDS AND VEGETATION
9-4-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the CITY OF OROFINO NOXIOUS WEEDS AND VEGETATION
ORDINANCE. (Ord. 781, 3-11-2014)
9-4-2: DEFINITIONS; ADOPTION BY REFERENCE:
All definitions identified in Idaho Code title 22, chapter 24 are hereby adopted by reference with like
effect as if recited at length.
CODE ENFORCEMENT OFFICER: The Orofino "building official", the "Orofino fire chief", or any "law
enforcement officer" for the city.
NOXIOUS WEED: Any plant having the potential to cause injury to public health, crops, livestock, land
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 201/315
or other property; and which is designated as noxious by the director of the department of agriculture.
RANK: Growing with excessive luxuriance; vigorous and tall of growth.
RIGHT OF WAY: That portion of property also referred as a boulevard, parkway, walkway, or
undeveloped property for the use of pedestrian traffic or utilities which is located adjacent to the
property owner and the city street.
TREE: Any plant materials commonly referred to as trees which at maturity would exceed a height of
more than thirty inches (30").
VEGETATION: Any plant materials including, but not limited to, those commonly referred to as grass,
weeds, volunteer shrubs, volunteer trees, shrubs and trees. (Ord. 781, 3-11-2014)
9-4-3: DECLARED NUISANCE:
The allowing or permitting of the rank growth of any vegetation or trees as well as the growth of any
designated noxious weeds within the city is hereby declared a nuisance. (Ord. 781, 3-11-2014)
9-4-4: ABATEMENT:
No person as the owner, occupant or person in charge or control of any property within the city shall:
A. Allow or permit any rank growth of vegetation, trees or the growth of any designated noxious
weed(s) upon such property or upon any areas adjacent to such property, from the edge of the
adjacent street paving, centerline of adjacent alley travelways and centerline of adjacent
undeveloped right of way;
B. Allow or permit any vegetation or tree growth to overhang below nine feet (9') above the right of
way area, from the edge of the travelway to the property line of the adjacent property or rest upon
the sidewalk and/or sidewalk space adjacent to such property so as to interfere in any manner with
the full, free and unobstructed use of such sidewalk or sidewalk space;
C. Allow or permit any vegetation growth within the right of way, from the edge of the travelway to the
property line of the adjacent property, which would obstruct the clear vision area of an intersection
or driveway. This subsection shall not apply to trees placed on the right of way and maintained
pursuant to the urban forestry program and/or pursuant to the authority of the director of public
works;
D. Allow or permit any vegetation or tree growth to overhang below fourteen feet (14'), above any
public travelway designated for motor vehicle traffic. Measurements shall be determined from the
centerline elevation of the adjacent travelway;
E. Allow or permit any vegetation or noxious weed growth upon such property to the extent that it
creates a fire hazard as defined by the international fire code as adopted by this code;
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 202/315
F. Allow or permit any vegetation, designated noxious weed or tree growth to the extent that it creates
a sight obstruction as defined in Idaho Code, section 49-221;
G. Allow or permit any tree infested with disease or insects to remain standing without application of
proper treatment(s) to correct and/or eliminate the disease or infestation. If said tree is determined
by the city forester to be dying or dead the tree shall be removed within ten (10) days after receipt
of written notice from the code enforcement officer, or within such additional extended time allowed
by the code enforcement officer. (Ord. 781, 3-11-2014)
9-4-5: ABATEMENT OF VIOLATION:
The code enforcement officer shall, no later than May 15 of each year, cause a notice to be published
in the official newspaper requiring all designated noxious weeds, rank vegetation, volunteer shrub
and/or tree, or tree growth to be properly controlled and/or eradicated upon any private property within
the city and upon any areas adjacent to such property as provided in section 9-4-4 of this chapter.
A. Notice To Abate Violation: Should any property located within the city limits of Orofino, Idaho
remain in violation of this chapter ten (10) days after publication of such notice, the code
enforcement officer shall serve notice upon the owner, person in control or contract purchaser of
said property describing the violation(s) and requiring the owner, person in control or contract
purchaser to eradicate and/or properly control any designated noxious weed, weeds, rank
vegetation, volunteer shrub and/or tree, or tree growth upon said property or adjacent areas as
provided in section 9-4-4 of this chapter. Such notice shall be accomplished by posting said notice
on the real property whereon the noxious weeds or rank vegetation should be eradicated and by
mail, addressed to said owner at his/her last address of record.
B. Properly Control: "Properly control" shall mean commonly used and specific methods of eradicating
and/or preventing the growth of broadleaf weeds, noxious weeds and other weed type vegetation
and/or undesirable volunteer trees along with commonly used and specific methods of caring for
and/or maintaining the growth of certain desirable vegetation commonly referred to as grass.
These methods include, but are not limited to:
1. The correct preparation of vegetation and/or undesirable volunteer trees for the application of
herbicides and/or the actual application of herbicides to vegetation and/or undesirable volunteer
trees, that are known to prevent, inhibit and/or eradicate the growth of specific vegetation
commonly referred to as weeds and volunteer trees.
2. The trimming, cutting, pruning and/or mowing of vegetation to a height that is correct for the
primary desirable vegetation present on the property and/or a height that will not be detrimental
to the healthy growth of the primary desirable vegetation present.
3. The pruning, cutting, and/or otherwise trimming of shrubs, trees and/or other vegetation in
manner that will prevent the same from interfering with any sidewalk area, sidewalk, right of way
or travelways by causing a physical obstruction and/or sight obstruction as defined by law.
4. In some instances the effective removal of vegetation, shrubs and/or trees may be required to
eliminate physical obstructions and/or sight obstructions present in the sidewalk, sidewalk area,
right of way and/or travelway.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 203/315
5. The mowing and/or cutting of vegetation in a prescribed manner, to a prescribed height and in
an area of prescribed width in order to establish a satisfactory fuel break in areas where an
actual fire hazard is determined to exist.
6. The turning over, plowing and/or otherwise breaking up of the soil in a prescribed manner and in
an area of prescribed width in order to establish a satisfactory fuel break in areas where an
actual fire hazard is determined to exist.
C. Action Upon Noncompliance: Upon the failure, neglect or refusal of any owner or contract
purchaser, after being notified as provided for in subsection A of this section, to properly control
and/or eradicate any designated noxious weed, weeds, rank vegetation, volunteer shrub or tree, or
tree growth upon said private property or adjacent right of way areas, as specified in section 9-4-4
of this chapter, within ten (10) days of the posting of notice on the real property, the code
enforcement officer is hereby authorized and empowered to cause the violation to be abated
and/or to issue citation for violations of this code.
D. Charges For Abatement Of Violations - Special Assessments: When the city has caused any
violation of section 9-4-3 of this chapter to be abated, as provided for hereinabove in this section,
then the actual cost for such abatement, plus an administrative fee and accrued interest at the rate
of not more than six percent (6%) per annum from the date of the completed abatement shall be
chargeable and assessable against the owner or contract purchaser of the subject property. All
such charges if not paid within thirty (30) days to the city clerk of the city of Orofino, Idaho, shall be
declared delinquent and may be certified to the tax collector of Clearwater County, Idaho, by the
city clerk and collected in the manner provided for in Idaho Code, section 50-1008. (Ord. 781, 3-
11-2014)
9-4-6: PENALTY FOR VIOLATION:
Any person or entity who owns or is in control of or is the contract purchaser of real property found to
be in violation of this chapter, shall be deemed to have committed a misdemeanor and for each
violation shall be fined a sum not exceeding three hundred dollars ($300.00) or by imprisonment in the
county jail for a term not to exceed six (6) months, or by both such fine and imprisonment. Each day
the real property remains in violation shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 781, 3-11-2014)
Chapter 5
MUNICIPAL SWIMMING POOL
9-5-1: OPERATION:
The Municipal swimming pool of the City shall be open to the public at all proper and reasonable
times, the opening date, hours of operation and closing date to be fixed annually by the Council. (Ord.
332, 5-9-1955)
9-5-2: RULES:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 204/315
The operation of the swimming pool shall be subject to the rules and regulations prescribed by this
Chapter, and to such other rules and regulations as the Council may from time to time adopt or
authorize. (Ord. 332, 5-9-1955)
9-5-3: MANAGER; DUTIES:
The Council shall appoint a swimming pool manager who shall be an employee of the City, and who
shall receive such salary as may be authorized by the Mayor and Council. The manager shall have
general supervision over the swimming pool and the operation of the same. It shall be the duty of the
manager to preserve order, to enforce all provisions of this Chapter and all rules and regulations
adopted or authorized, and the manager is hereby authorized to exclude from the swimming pool any
person violating the same. (Ord. 332, 5-9-1955)
9-5-4: EMPLOYEES:
The Council shall appoint such employees, assistants, lifeguards and attendants as may be required
for the purpose of administering the provisions of this Chapter and of operating the swimming pool, all
of whom shall be under the immediate direction and supervision of the pool manager. (Ord. 332, 5-9-
1955)
9-5-5: DISEASED PERSONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person who is afflicted with a contagious or infectious disease to enter the
swimming pool; and the manager is hereby authorized to require a certificate of a licensed physician
that any person applying for admission to the pool is free from any such contagious or infectious
disease. (Ord. 332, 5-9-1955)
9-5-6: POLLUTION OF POOL:
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw or place in the water or the pool any stones, debris, refuse
or discarded substances of any kind, or in any manner wilfully to pollute the water of the pool. (Ord.
332, 5-9-1955)
9-5-7: ANIMALS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place any animals in the water of the pool or in the pool area.
(Ord. 332, 5-9-1955)
9-5-8: POOL HOURS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to enter the water of the pool except during the prescribed operating
hours and while the manager or a lifeguard is present and on duty. (Ord. 332, 5-9-1955)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 205/315
9-5-9: PAYMENT OF CHARGES REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to enter the pool or pool gates without first paying the established
charge to the cashier. (Ord. 332, 5-9-1955)
9-5-10: CHILDREN:
It shall be unlawful for any child under the age of seven (7) years to enter the pool unless
accompanied by a parent, guardian or some adult who shall be responsible for such child. (Ord. 332,
5-9-1955)
9-5-11: POOL CHARGES:
The charges prescribed for the use of the swimming pool shall be as determined from time to time by
the Mayor and Council. (Ord. 409, 5-23-1967)
Chapter 6
CEMETERIES
9-6-1: HILL CEMETERY:
The Hill Cemetery is hereby closed to the sale of lots therein. (Ord. 349, 3-25-1959)
9-6-2: RIVERSIDE CEMETERY; BURIAL CHARGES:
The new cemetery shall be known as the Riverside Cemetery and each lot for the burial of dead
human bodies therein shall be sold for a price established by resolution of the City Council, with no
reduction for purchasing more than one lot in a block; provided, however, that a one-half (1/2) lot for
the interment not requiring a grave in excess of three feet (3') in length, shall be sold for a separate
price as determined by resolution. (Ord. 566, 1-11-1983)
9-6-3: PERMIT REQUIRED FOR BURIAL; SEXTON'S CHARGES:
Before the City shall cause the sexton to open a grave, burial permit shall be presented to the
undertaker, showing proper compliance with the laws of the State relative to the burial of human
bodies; and, upon the presentation thereof, and the payment of the price of the burial lot, together with
the sexton's charges as established by resolution, for the opening and closing thereof; provided,
however, if the interment does not require a grave in excess of three feet (3') in length, a separate
charge will be determined by resolution; provided, further, that should the interment be made on a
Saturday, an additional charge as determined by resolution, shall be made for the service and no
person shall be allowed or permitted to open or close a grave on Sunday or any other legal holiday.
No person shall be allowed or permitted to open or close a grave except under the order of the sexton
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 206/315
designated by the Council. In the event that any of the provisions hereof are violated, the person so
violating the same shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 566, 1-11-1983)
9-6-4: BURIAL REGULATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for the burial at separate times of more than one human body in one grave lot;
provided, however, that if two (2) dead human bodies are buried in the same casket as one interment,
this shall not apply. (Ord. 212, 1-12-1940)
9-6-5: PURCHASE OF LOTS FOR RESALE PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to purchase lots or blocks in either cemetery for the purpose of
resale thereof; provided, however, that nothing contained herein shall prohibit a party who has
purchased lots or a block in said cemeteries, in good faith, from disposing of said lots or portions of a
block to others, in good faith, for the burial of members of the purchaser's family therein, or to prohibit
any society or fraternal organizations from purchasing blocks for burial of the members of that
organization. (Ord. 212, 1-12-1940)
9-6-6: HEADSTONE AND DECORATION REGULATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place or cause to be placed on any cemetery burial lot any
headstone or decorative marker that shall extend more than one-half inch (1/2") above ground level,
except that portions of the cemetery currently plotted, and of the effective date of this Section, are
exempt from this provision and aboveground headstones shall be permitted in said currently plotted
section, provided such headstones are permanently affixed to a solid base level with the ground and
extending a minimum of six inches (6") in all directions from the headstone. It shall also be unlawful
for any person to locate or cause to be located, on a permanent basis, on any burial lot, any tree,
shrub, fence, vase or any other decorative item. Decorative items may be placed on burial lots, on a
temporary basis, for a period not to exceed seven (7) days. Any decorative item not removed from a
burial lot within a seven (7) day period shall be discarded by the City. (Ord. 600, 4-23-1985)
Chapter 7
NUMBERING OF BUILDINGS
9-7-1: SYSTEM OF NUMBERING:
For the purpose of numbering for distribution of mail, the various lots, pieces and parcels of land within
the corporate limits, the following system is adopted:
A. East And West: As a base for numbering east and west, a line shall be established as commencing
at the south boundary of the City limits thence northwesterly along the center line of Main Street to
a point where the same intersects the center line of Michigan Avenue; thence northwesterly along
Michigan Avenue to a point where the same intersects the right-of-way line of the Northern Pacific
Railway Company; thence northwesterly along the said right-of-way line to a point where the same
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 207/315
intersects the City limits. A separate number shall be given for each approximate twelve feet (12')
of lot front and all blocks easterly or westerly from said line shall bear the same number in
hundreds and those westerly from said line shall be numbered as west, and accordingly as the
number of said block is east or west of said base line.
B. North And South: As a base for numbering north and south, a line shall be established as
commencing at a point in the meander line of the Clearwater where the same would be intersected
by Michigan Avenue extended, then extending easterly along said center line to the eastern
boundary of the City limits. A separate number shall be assigned for each approximate twelve feet
(12') of lot frontage and lots facing on A and B streets lying south of Michigan shall bear the prefix
South A and B, respectively, and those facing the same streets and lying north of Michigan shall
bear the prefix North, respectively, and all lots in the same block shall bear the same number in
hundreds and the blocks shall be numbered in hundreds according to the number of the block
north or south of said base. (Res., 4-11-1927)
Chapter 8
MUNICIPAL AIRPORT
9-8-1: LOCATION AND ESTABLISHMENT:
The City is the owner and operator of that Municipal Airport located in Lots 9, 10, 11 and 12 in Section
1, Township 36 north, Range 1 E.B.M. and the same is maintained as a public airport.
An exclusive lease or permission to use or occupy the Municipal Airport shall not be granted to any
person, but said airport shall at all times be open for the use of the public for air navigation purposes.
Provided, however, permission may be granted for the establishing of airport facilities such as
hangars, machine shops or gasoline stations needed or used in air navigation. (Ord. 255, 2-14-1949)
9-8-2: FEES:
The airport shall be open for the landing and taking off of licensed aircraft as provided by the laws of
the United States and of the State of Idaho. Provided, however, that there shall be charged and
collected the following fees and taxes for the use of said airport:
A. Commercial Purpose: For the use of said airport by any person for commercial purposes, the sum
of fifteen dollars ($15.00) per month, which said charge shall be in addition to all the other charges
provided for by this Chapter. As used herein, the term "commercial purposes" means the operation
of any aircraft for a profit to the operator.
B. Leasing Of Ground: For the leasing of ground for constructing and maintaining a hangar thereon,
the rental charge of the ground shall be one cent ($0.01) per square foot when used only for
private storage, and one and one-half cents ($0.015) per square foot when used for commercial
purposes. Such charge shall be paid annually and no lease shall be for less than two thousand
(2,000) square feet, and no lease shall be for longer than five (5) years, and shall require full
compliance with this Chapter; and when such hangar is removed, the ground shall be restored to
its present condition.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 208/315
C. Gasoline Sold Or Dispensed: For all gasoline sold or dispensed from said airport, a tax in the sum
of two cents ($0.02) per gallon, the said tax to be paid by any dealer or other person selling or
dispensing gasoline from the said airport, on or before the fifth day of each month, for all gasoline
so sold or dispensed during the preceding calendar month. Any such dealer or person so selling
and dispensing gasoline from the said airport shall, with each remittance of tax monies, submit to
the Council a statement of the number of gallons of gasoline sold or dispensed by him during the
preceding calendar month.
D. Right To Limit Number Of Planes: The Mayor and Council, by resolution duly passed, reserve the
right to limit the number of planes to be maintained and stored on the said airport, and also the
number of hangars and the size thereof. Provided, that this clause shall not be so construed as to
grant any person the right to keep or store, or lease hangar space on said airport sufficient to
create a monopoly thereof. (Ord. 372, 6-14-1962, eff. retroactive to 6-1-1962)
9-8-3: RENTAL AND CONSTRUCTION PERMITS:
All buildings now located on said airport are declared the property of the City and before any person
shall have the right to the use or occupancy of any such building or structure, permission must be
secured from the Mayor and Council and upon such terms, rentals and conditions as may then be
determined and no permission for such use shall be made for a period of longer than one year, and
such use shall be subject to cancellation upon thirty (30) days' notice or upon any breach of the
permission granted. The mayor and council may permit the use of certain ground for the erection of a
private hangar, machine shop, gas station and pumps. Provided that, before any such facilities may be
built, constructed or installed, detailed plans thereof are to be filed with the clerk, showing the type of
construction and location. All permits must be in writing. No permit for the use of land shall be granted
which will, in the opinion of the mayor and council, interfere with the use of the runways or present
facilities of the airport. Such permission shall be limited as to time and are not transferable and are at
all times subject to cancellation for breach thereof. Each person granted permission to establish and
install facilities shall pay to the clerk reasonable monthly rental for the use of the ground, as the
council may determine. All such rentals shall be equal for like permits, subject, however, to the right of
the council to be the sole judge of the necessity and fitness of such grant or grants, but this shall not
be construed as to give the council the right to place such restrictions that would grant exclusive right
to concessions and any person and any concession, other than private hangar, is open to the public
and the charges made and services rendered shall be equal to all persons asking for the same. Any
discrimination given or shown by any person holding a concession permit shall constitute a violation of
the permit and, upon conviction thereof, the party found guilty shall have the permit canceled and be
subject to a fine of not over one hundred dollars ($100.00) and may be denied thereafter the use of
the airport. (Ord. 255, 2-14-1949)
9-8-4: FEES FOR TEMPORARY USE:
A. Temporary Barnstorming: In the event any person shall bring to said airport aircraft for the purpose
of temporary barnstorming and not regularly maintained at said airport, they shall pay to the city
such fees as may be determined by the council. Such person shall make report and payment daily
for the use of said airport and, if such payment and report is not made, they shall be denied the
use of the airport for such purposes.
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 209/315
B. Violation: The council reserves the right to designate some person to inspect the books of any
person using said airport as herein provided and, if it is found that false statements are made or
reports are not made, then such person making such false statement or failing to report shall, upon
conviction, and in addition to being prohibited from the use of said airport, be subject to
imprisonment in the city jail for not more than thirty (30) days or a fine not exceeding one hundred
dollars ($100.00), or both, and such action shall be tried before the police judge.
C. Occasional Business; Emergency Landings: No charge for the use of the airport shall apply to
aircraft stationed elsewhere and landing at the local airport for the purpose of discharging
passengers or cargo taken on elsewhere or when only an occasional passenger or cargo is
loaded, nor shall it apply to emergency landings or landing of aircraft during an emergency or for
loading or unloading firefighters. The council shall be the sole judge whether the landing is
occasional or as a regular business. (Ord. 255, 2-14-1949)
D. Commercial Use Of Airport: The city council shall set by resolution the daily fees for the temporary
use of airport facilities when an individual, group, organization, company, corporation, or other
entity uses the airport for private, commercial or business purposes. Prior permission from the city
is required before any use of the airport is granted. (Ord. 697, 5-22-2000)
9-8-5: MAINTENANCE AND CARE; RESPONSIBILITY FOR DAMAGE:
All persons granted permits to use or maintain aircraft upon the airport or granted concessions
thereon shall be responsible for the proper maintenance thereof and care of the concession. Any
damage or expense caused by the negligence of any such person to properly keep the same shall
give the city the right to repair such damage or clean up the grounds and the cost thereof shall be
repaid to the city. Failure to repair or account to the city shall be grounds for refusal of the use of said
airport, but such refusal shall not prevent the city from suing for and recovering for said damage. (Ord.
255, 2-14-1949)
9-8-6: RIGHTS OF CITY TO SEIZE AIRCRAFT:
All persons having aircraft on said airport, or having equipment to conduct and operate concessions,
by granting of the permit to use the airport or establish concessions shall grant, and by the taking out
of such permit they do grant, to the city a lien thereon for the payment of any and all charges
heretofore provided, as well as penalties, and the city has the right, through its officers, to seize such
aircraft or equipment and hold the same until such charges are paid. In the event aircraft or equipment
of any person are so seized, they shall have the right to a hearing before the mayor and council by
making a demand therefor in writing, duly verified, setting forth the grounds of protest and serving the
same upon the mayor and clerk. When such a notice is served, the mayor shall call a special meeting
of the council within ten (10) days to hear and consider said protest and their decision shall be final.
Provided that, pending such hearing the person whose property is held shall have the right to deposit
with the clerk security in an amount equal to the amount claimed due, with costs, and when such
security is so filed, the property shall be released and such bond shall be in lieu of the property. (Ord.
255, 2-14-1949)
9-8-7: AIRPORT MAINTENANCE FUND:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 210/315
All fees, fines and charges obtained by virtue of this chapter shall be paid into the airport maintenance
fund and used for the upkeep and maintenance of said airport and paid out upon the warrant after
approval of the council. (Ord. 255, 2-14-1949)
9-8-8: PERMISSION TO USE AIRPORT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to trespass upon the airport grounds without permission, other than
the right of ingress and egress in going to or from the aircraft or concessions in the usual manner.
(Ord. 255, 2-14-1949)
9-8-9: VEHICLE AND AIRCRAFT TRAFFIC REGULATED:
Vehicle and aircraft traffic on the municipal airport shall be regulated by resolution of the council; a
copy of all regulations shall be posted in the office of the airport manager, and copies of the
regulations shall be available from the airport manager. (Ord. 453, 12-13-1971)
9-8-10: STORAGE OF AVIATION FUEL:
No person shall bring aviation fuel upon or store aviation fuel upon the municipal airport without the
prior approval of the city council. (Ord. 453, 12-13-1971)
9-8-11: OPERATION OF FLIGHT TRAINING BUSINESS:
No person shall engage in the furnishing of flight training or instruction for a fee or other consideration
without first applying for and obtaining a permit from the council and providing the following
improvements and facilities, which shall be subject to the approval of the council:
A. Evidence Of Compliance: Each applicant shall have complied with all applicable laws, rules and
regulations of appropriate agencies and shall present evidence of such compliance to the council.
B. Lease Of Lots: Each applicant shall have leased from the city no fewer than two (2) standard airport
lots.
C. Liability Insurance: Each applicant shall provide liability insurance by a carrier and in amounts
acceptable and with riders protecting the city.
D. Classroom Space And Related Facilities: Each applicant shall provide adequate classroom space
and related facilities including restrooms, telephone and parking facilities.
E. Acquaint Students With Rules: Each applicant shall agree to fully acquaint his students with all
ordinances, rules and regulations of the city with regard to the use of the municipal airport and with
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 211/315
regard to aircraft and vehicular traffic on and about the municipal airport. (Ord. 453, 12-13-1971)
9-8-12: AIRCRAFT CHARTER OR AIR TAXI OPERATIONS:
No person shall engage in the aircraft charter or air taxi business, or furnish aircraft charter or air taxi
services for a fee or other consideration without first applying for and obtaining a permit from the
council and providing the following improvements and facilities subject to the approval of the council:
A. Lease Of Lots: Each applicant shall have under lease a minimum of three (3) standard airport lots
from the city for the purpose of providing customer parking, aircraft parking and aircraft taxiing.
B. Evidence Of Compliance: Each applicant shall have complied with all applicable laws, rules and
regulations and shall furnish evidence thereof to the council.
C. Insurance: Each applicant shall obtain and furnish evidence to the council of insurance with an
acceptable company, in acceptable amounts with acceptable riders to protect the city.
D. Building And Facilities; Office Hours: Each applicant shall provide a building containing not less
than seven hundred eighty (780) square feet including public areas, restrooms, telephone and
other related facilities. Each applicant must maintain regular office hours with personnel on duty
during those hours as may be required by the council. (Ord. 453, 12-13-1971)
9-8-13: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction thereof, shall be subject to such penalties as are provided by law. (Ord. 453, 12-13-1971)
Chapter 9
EXCAVATIONS
9-9-1: PERMIT REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to tunnel under or to make any excavation in any street, alley or
other public place in the City without having obtained a permit as herein required, or without complying
with the provisions of this Chapter, or in violation of or variance from the terms of any such permit.
(Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-2: APPLICATION FOR PERMIT:
Applications for such permit shall be made to the City Clerk, and shall describe the location of the
intended excavation or tunnel, the size thereof, the purpose therefor, and the person doing the actual
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 212/315
excavating work and the name of the person for whom or which the work is being done, and shall
contain an agreement that the applicant will comply with all ordinances and laws relating to the work to
be done. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-3: LIABILITY INSURANCE:
No permit shall be issued unless and until the applicant therefor has filed with the Clerk a certification
of effective liability insurance conditioned to indemnify the City for any loss, liability or damage that
may result or accrue from or because of the making, existence or manner of guarding or constructing
any such tunnel or excavation. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-4: DEPOSIT:
No such permit shall be issued unless and until the applicant therefor has deposited with the Clerk a
cash deposit in the sum of fifty dollars ($50.00), if no pavement is involved, and the sum of one
hundred dollars ($100.00), if the excavation is in a paved area, to ensure the proper restoration of the
ground and laying of the pavement, if any. From this deposit shall be deducted the expense to the City
of relaying the surface of the ground or pavement and of making the refill if this is done by the City or
at its expense, and the balance shall be returned to the applicant without interest after the tunnel or
excavation is completely refilled and the surface or pavement is restored. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-5: MANNER OF EXCAVATING:
A. Compliance With Terms Of Permit: It shall be unlawful to make any such excavation or tunnel in
any way contrary to or at variance with the terms of the permit therefor. Proper bracing shall be
maintained to prevent the collapse of adjoining ground; and in excavations, the excavation shall
not have anywhere below the surface any portion which extends beyond the opening at the
surface.
B. Damage To Pipes, Cable Or Conduits; Notice: No injury shall be done to any pipes, cables or
conduits in the making of such excavations or tunnels; and notice shall be given to the persons
maintaining any such pipes, cables or conduits or to the City department or officer charged with the
care thereof, which are or may be endangered or affected by the making of such excavation or
tunnel before such pipes, cables or conduits shall be disturbed.
C. Damage To Trees Or Shrubs: No unnecessary damage or injury shall be done to any tree or shrub,
or the roots thereof. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-6: SIDEWALKS:
If any sidewalk is blocked by any such work, a temporary sidewalk shall be constructed or provided
which shall be safe for travel and convenient for users. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-7: RESTORING SURFACE:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 213/315
A. Restore To Original Condition: Any person making any excavation or tunnel in or under any public
street, alley or other public place in the City shall restore the surface to its original condition.
B. Repairs Made And Surfaces Relaid: Any opening in a paved or improved portion of a street shall be
repaired and the surface relaid by the applicant, in compliance with the ordinances of the City and
under the supervision of the Street Superintendent. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-8: SUPERVISION:
The Street Superintendent shall from time to time inspect or cause to be inspected all excavations and
tunnels being made in or under any public street, alley or other public place in the City to see to the
enforcement of the provisions of this Chapter. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-9: PROTECTIVE MEASURES:
A. Maintain Barriers And Warning Devices: It shall be the duty of every person cutting or making an
excavation in or upon any public place, to place and maintain barriers and warning devices
necessary for safety of the general public.
B. Maintain Normal Traffic Conditions: The permittee shall take appropriate measures to assure that
during the performance of the excavation work, traffic conditions as near normal as possible shall
be maintained at all times so as to minimize inconvenience to the occupants of the adjoining
property and to the general public. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-10: CLEANUP:
As the excavation work progresses, all streets shall be thoroughly cleaned of all rubbish, excess earth,
rock and other debris resulting from such work. All cleanup operations at the location of such
excavation shall be accomplished at the expense of the permittee and shall be completed to the
satisfaction of the Street Superintendent. From time to time, as may be ordered by the Street
Superintendent, and in any event immediately after the completion of the said work, the permittee
shall, at his own or its own expense, clean up and remove all refuse and unused materials of any kind
resulting from said work, and upon failure to do so within twenty four (24) hours after having been
notified to do so by the Street Superintendent, said work may be done by the Street Superintendent,
and the cost thereof charged to the permittee. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
9-9-11: PROMPT COMPLETION OF WORK:
After an excavation is commenced, the permittee shall prosecute with diligence and expedition all
excavation work covered by the excavation permit and shall promptly complete such work and restore
the street to its original condition, so as not to obstruct the public place or travel thereon more than is
reasonably necessary. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 214/315
9-9-12: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this Chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and a
separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or
continues. (Ord. 438, 12-4-1970)
Chapter 10
AVISTA CORPORATION FRANCHISE
9-10-1: PURPOSE:
Avista Corporation (hereinafter referred to as "Grantee"), its successors and assigns, is hereby
granted a franchise by the city of Orofino (hereinafter referred to as "Grantor" or the "City") for the
purposes identified herein and subject to the terms and conditions outlined in this chapter. (Ord. 707,
11-12-2001)
9-10-2: FRANCHISE GRANTED:
Grantor hereby grants to grantee, its successors and assigns, the right, power, privilege and authority
to enter upon all roads, rights of way, streets, alleys, public places or structures lying within the
boundaries of grantor and owned or maintained by grantor, to locate, construct, operate and maintain
poles, wires, underground cables and all necessary or desirable appurtenances for the purpose of
transmitting and distributing electricity. This franchise shall allow for the placement of such facilities as
may be necessary to provide service within the city and surrounding areas. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-3: TERM:
The rights, privileges and franchise hereby granted to, and conferred upon the grantee shall, unless
this franchise be sooner terminated as herein provided, extend for a term of twenty five (25) years
from the date of written acceptance hereof by the grantee. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-4: TRIMMING/REMOVAL OF TREES:
The right of grantee to maintain its lines, facilities and appurtenances shall include the right, as
exercised in grantee's sole discretion, to utilize an integrated vegetation management program,
including the right to cut, trim or remove any and all trees, brush or shrubs growing in, on, or hanging
over any city roads, rights of way, streets, alleys or city property that interfere with or may interfere
with grantee's facilities, including wires, poles, conduits or other apparatus of grantee, its successors
and assigns. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-5: RIGHT OF EXCAVATION:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 215/315
For the purpose of carrying into effect the privileges granted hereunder, grantee is authorized at any
time to make all necessary excavations in the streets, alleys, roads, rights of way and public grounds
within the franchised area, but such excavation shall be carried out with reasonable dispatch and with
as little interference with or inconvenience to the rights of the public as may be feasible. Grantee shall
restore all streets, alleys, roads, rights of way and public grounds to a standard as agreed upon for
conditions of safety and use after excavation. In case any obstruction caused by grantee shall remain
longer than seven (7) days after notice to remove it, or in case of neglect by grantee to safeguard any
dangerous places, grantor may remove such obstruction or safeguard such dangerous places at the
expense of the grantee. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-6: NONINTERFERENCE WITH EXISTING FACILITIES:
All construction, installation, repair or relocation of lines and appurtenances performed by grantee
along or under the roads, rights of way or properties subject to this franchise shall be done in such a
manner as not to interfere with the construction and maintenance of other utilities, public or private,
drains, drainage ditches and structures, irrigation ditches and structures located therein, nor with the
grading or improvement of such roads, rights of way or other public property subject to this franchise.
(Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-7: NECESSARY CONSTRUCTION/MAINTENANCE BY GRANTOR:
The laying, construction, operation and maintenance of grantee's lines and appurtenances authorized
by this franchise shall not preclude the grantor, its agents or its contractors, from blasting, excavating,
or doing other necessary road work contiguous to the said lines and facilities of grantee, provided that
grantee shall be given not less than five (5) days' notice of said blasting or other work, and provided
further that the grantor, its agents and contractors shall be liable for any damages, including any
consequential damages to third parties, caused by said work to any installations belonging to grantee.
(Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-8: CONDUCT OF GRANTEE'S BUSINESS:
The grantor shall have the right to make and enforce reasonable rules and regulations pertaining to
the conduct of the grantee's business. Service shall be supplied to the grantor and its inhabitants in
accordance with the grantee's rules and regulations and tariffs filed or hereafter filed with the
appropriate regulatory body of this state having jurisdiction over the grantee. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-9: RIGHTS OF INGRESS/EGRESS:
The grantee, its agents and employees, shall have the right and power to ingress and egress upon its
customers' properties for the purpose of installing, servicing and maintaining its facilities including the
testing and reading of service meters. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-10: VACATION OF PROPERTIES BY GRANTOR:
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 216/315
If, at any time, the grantor shall vacate any road, right of way or other public property which is subject
to rights granted by this franchise, to the extent permitted by law, such vacation shall be subject to the
reservation of a perpetual easement in favor of grantor for the purpose of operating and maintaining
the facilities of the grantee and other public utilities. Such easement shall also expressly prohibit any
use of the vacated properties, which will interfere with grantor's ability to provide grantee's full
enjoyment of its rights under this franchise. Grantor shall also continue to permit grantee to operate
and maintain its facilities in or on the vacated property consistent with and subject to this franchise.
(Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-11: RELOCATION OF FACILITIES:
Grantor shall notify grantee of any intended or expected requirement or request to relocate grantee's
facilities as early as practicable, but not later than one hundred twenty (120) days prior to any such
relocation when the requirement or request could have been foreseen by that date. Grantor shall
endeavor to cause any such relocation to be consistent with any applicable long term development
plan or projection of grantor or approved by grantor. If, at any time, the grantor shall cause or require
the alteration or the improvement of any road, highway or right of way wherein grantee maintains
facilities subject to this franchise by grading or regrading, planking or paving the same, changing the
grade, altering, changing, repairing or relocating the same or by constructing drainage or sanitary
sewer facilities, the grantee upon written notice from the grantor shall, with all convenient speed,
change the location or readjust the elevation of its system and other facilities so that the same shall
not interfere with such work and so that such equipment and facilities shall conform to such new
grades or routes as may be established. The relocation of grantee's facilities shall be at the sole
expense of grantee unless: a) the improvement was not paid for solely with public funds, in which
case the grantor agrees to make reasonable efforts to facilitate an agreement between the adjoining
property owners or developers to pay for the costs of relocation; or b) grantor has failed to provide the
required advance notice in which case any and all excess costs caused by the failure to provide such
notice shall be paid by grantor. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-12: PRESERVATION OF GRANTOR'S RIGHTS TO CONTROL:
The grantor, in granting this franchise, does not waive any rights which it may now have or may
hereafter acquire with respect to road rights of way or other property of grantor under this franchise,
and this franchise shall not be construed to deprive the grantor of any such powers, rights or privileges
which it now has or may hereafter require to regulate the use of and to control the grantor's roads,
rights of way and other public property covered by this franchise. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
9-10-13: EMERGENCY REMOVAL OF GRANTOR:
The grantor reserves the right to remove any such wires, poles, or apparatus ("Grantee's facilities")
herein provided for in case of general conflagration or in other cases of extreme emergency where
there is neither the time nor the opportunity for grantee to perform such work. Grantor shall use
reasonable care in the exercise of such emergency powers. Grantor shall indemnify and hold
harmless the grantee, its successors and assigns, against any and all property damage, personal
injury, death, or other liability to third parties sustained as a result of the negligent exercise of such
reserved emergency powers, and shall, at its expense, restore grantee's facilities removed as a result
of such exercise. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
6/5/2019 Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
https://www.sterlingcodifiers.com/codebook/index.php?book_id=1077 217/315
9-10-14: NONEXCLUSIVE FRANCHISE:
This franchise shall not be deemed to be an exclusive franchise. It shall in no manner prohibit the
grantor from granting other franchises of a like nature or franchises to other public or private utilities
under, along, across, over and upon any of grantor's roads, rights of way or other property of grantor
subject to this franchise and shall in no way prevent or prohibit the grantor from constructing, altering,
maintaining or using any of said roads, rights of way, drainage structures of facilities, irrigation
structures of facilities, or any other property of grantor or affect its jurisdiction over such property to
make all necessary changes, relocations, repairs, maintenance, etc., insofar as the grantor may deem
fit. (Ord. 707, 11-12-2001)
